PREFACE
This code of the Village of Buckingham, as supplemented, contains ordinances up
to and including ordinance passed September 5, 2023. Ordinances of the Village
adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code to the
extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the Village
office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the code has
been amended, superseded or repealed.
American Legal Publishing
Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCE NO. 18-3
   AN ORDINANCE ADOPTING
   THE VILLAGE OF BUCKINGHAM, BUCKINGHAM VILLAGE CODE
BE IT ORDAINED by the President and Board of Trustees of the Village of
Buckingham, Illinois as follows:
   Section 1: Pursuant to the provisions of 65 ILCS 5/1-2-3, and from and after
the date of passage of this ordinance, the Village Code of the Village of
Buckingham, Illinois prepared by Sterling Codifiers, containing the compilation
of all ordinances of a general nature together with the changes made to said
ordinances, under the direction of the governing body of the Village, shall be
accepted in all courts without question as the official code and law of the
Village as enacted by the Village President and Board of Trustees.
   Section 2: There is hereby adopted, as a method of perpetual codification,
the loose-leaf type of binding together with the continuous supplement service,
provided by Sterling Codifiers, whereby each newly adopted ordinance of a
general and permanent nature amending, altering, adding or deleting provisions
of the official Village Code is identified by the proper catchline and is
inserted in the proper place in each of the official copies, one copy of which
shall be maintained in the office of the Village Clerk, certified as to
correctness and available for inspection at any and all times that said office
is regularly open.
   Section 3: All ordinances of a general nature included in this official
Village Code shall be considered as a continuation of said ordinance provision
and the fact that some provisions have been deliberately eliminated by the
governing body shall not serve to cause any interruption in the continuous
effectiveness of ordinances included in said official Village Code. All
ordinances of a special nature, such as tax levy ordinances, bond ordinances,
franchises, vacating ordinances and annexation ordinances shall continue in
full force and effect unless specifically repealed or amended by a provision of
the Village Code. Such ordinances are not intended to be included in the
official Village Code.
   Section 4: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to
change or amend by additions or deletions, any part or portion of such Village
Code, or to insert or delete pages or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper
with such Village Code in any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the
Village to be misrepresented thereby.
   Section 5: Any person violating any of the provisions of the Village Code
hereby adopted shall be fined an amount not to exceed seven hundred fifty
dollars ($750.00), and imprisonment not to exceed six (6) months.
   Section 6: All ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict herewith, are,
to the extent of such conflict, hereby repealed.
   Section 7: This ordinance and the Village Code adopted by the same shall be
recorded and shall be in full force and effect from and after its passage,
approval and publication in pamphlet form as provided by law.
PASSED this 7th day of August, 2018.
APPROVED this 7th day of August, 2018.
/s/      
Village President
ATTEST:
/s/      
Village Clerk
Roll Call Vote:
AYES: 5
NAYS: 0
ABSENT: 1
TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
BUCKINGHAM VILLAGE CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Acceptance
1-1-3: Amendments
1-1-4: Code Alterations
1-1-1: TITLE:
Upon adoption by the Board of Trustees, this Code is hereby declared to be and
shall hereafter constitute the official Village Code of Buckingham. This Code
of ordinances shall be known and cited as the BUCKINGHAM VILLAGE CODE and is
hereby published by authority of the Board of Trustees and shall be
supplemented to incorporate the most recent legislation of the Village as
provided in section
1-1-3 of this chapter. Any reference to the number of any section contained
herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the same number, its
appropriate chapter and title headings, and to the general penalty clause
relating thereto, as well as to the section itself, when reference is made to
this Code by title in any legal documents. (2018 Code)
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
This Code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received
without further proof in all courts and in administrative tribunals of the
State as the ordinances of the Village of general and permanent effect, except
the excluded ordinances enumerated in section
1-2-1 of this title. (2018 Code)
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
Any ordinance amending this Code shall set forth the title, chapter and section
numbers of the section or sections to be amended, and this shall constitute
sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement pertaining to the
amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this Code. All such
amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to the
codifier, and the said ordinance material shall be prepared for insertion in
its proper place in each copy of this Code. Each such replacement page shall be
properly identified and shall be inserted in each individual copy of this Code.
(2018 Code)
1-1-4: CODE ALTERATIONS:
It shall be deemed unlawful for any person to alter, change, replace or deface
in any way any section or any page of this Code in such a manner that the
meaning of any phrase or order may be changed or omitted. Replacement pages may
be inserted according to the official instructions when so authorized by the
Board of Trustees. The Village Clerk shall see that the replacement pages are
properly inserted in the official copies maintained in the Office of the Clerk.
Any person having in his custody an official copy of this Code shall make every
effort to maintain said Code in an up to date and efficient manner. He shall
see to the immediate insertion of new or replacement pages when such are
delivered to him or made available to him through the Office of the Village
Clerk. Said Code books, while in actual possession of officials and other
interested persons, shall be and remain the property of the Village and shall
be returned to the Office of the Clerk when directed so to do by order of the
Board of Trustees. (2018 Code)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Court Proceedings
1-2-3: Severability Clause
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
All general ordinances of the Village passed prior to the adoption of this Code
are hereby repealed, except such as are included in this Code or are by
necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to the saving
clauses contained in the following sections), and excluding the following
ordinances which are not hereby repealed:
   A.   Tax levy ordinances;
   B.   Appropriation ordinances;
   C.   Ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations;
   D.   Franchise ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to
persons or corporations;
   E.   Contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants;
   F.   Salary ordinances;
   G.   Ordinances establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other
public places;
   H.   Improvement ordinances;
   I.   Bond ordinances;
   J.   Ordinances relating to elections;
   K.   Ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or
from the Village; and
   L.   All special ordinances. (2018 Code)
1-2-2: COURT PROCEEDINGS:
   A.   Prior Acts: No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a
former ordinance, whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not,
as to any offense committed against such former ordinance or as to any act
done, any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued
or claim arising under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect
any such offense or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or
punishment so incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new
ordinance takes effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform
to the ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding, so far as
practicable. If any penalty, forfeiture or punishment may be mitigated by any
provision of a new ordinance, such provision may be, by consent of the party
affected, applied to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes
effect.
   B.   Extend To All Repeals: This section shall extend to all repeals, either
by express words or implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making
any new provisions upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
   C.   Current Pending Actions: Nothing contained in this chapter shall be
construed as abating any action now pending under or by virtue of any general
ordinance of the Village herein repealed, and the provisions of all general
ordinances contained in this Code shall be deemed to be continuing provisions
and not a new enactment of the same provisions; nor shall this chapter be
deemed as discontinuing, abating, modifying or altering any penalty accrued or
to accrue, or as affecting the liability of any person, firm or corporation, or
as waiving any right of the Village under any ordinance or provision thereof in
force at the time of the adoption of this Code. (2018 Code)
1-2-3: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
If any section, subsection, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase of this Code,
or any codes or portions of codes adopted herein by reference, is for any
reason held to be unconstitutional or invalid or ineffective by any court of
competent jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity or
effectiveness of the remaining portions of this Code, or any codes or portions
of codes adopted herein by reference. The Village Board of Trustees hereby
declares that it would have passed each section, subsection, paragraph,
sentence, clause or phrase thereof irrespective of the fact that any one or
more sections, subsections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses or phrases be
declared unconstitutional, invalid or ineffective. (2018 Code)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS; INTERPRETATION
SECTION:
1-3-1: General Rules Of Interpretation
1-3-2: General Definitions
1-3-3: Catchlines
1-3-1: GENERAL RULES OF INTERPRETATION:
   A.   Liberal Construction: All general provisions, terms, phrases and
expressions contained in this Code shall be liberally construed in order that
the true intent and meaning of the Mayor and Village Board of Trustees may be
fully carried out.
   B.   Minimum Requirements: In the interpretation and application of any
provision of this Code, it shall be held to be the minimum requirement adopted
for the promotion of the public health, safety and general welfare.
   C.   Delegation Of Authority: Whenever a provision appears requiring the
head of a department or some other Village officer to do some act or perform
some duty, it is to be construed to authorize the head of the department or
other officer to designate, delegate and authorize subordinates to perform the
required act or perform the duty unless the terms of the provision or section
specify otherwise.
   D.   Gender: The use of any gender based pronoun should not be construed to
be gender biased, but is only used for grammatical simplicity.
   E.   May; Shall: The word "may" is permissive; the word "shall" is
mandatory.
   F.   Nontechnical And Technical Words: Words and phrases shall be construed
according to the common and approved usage of the language, but technical words
and phrases and such others as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate
meaning in law shall be construed and understood according to such meaning.
   G.   Number: A word importing the singular number only may extend and be
applied to several persons and things as well as to one person and thing.
   H.   Officers And Employees Generally: Whenever any officer or employee is
referred to by title only, such reference shall be construed as if followed by
the words "of the Village of Buckingham".
   I.   Tense: Words used in the past or present tense include the future as
well as the past and present.
   J.   Ordinance: The word "ordinance" contained in the ordinances of the
Village has been changed in the content of this Code to "title", "chapter",
"section" and/or "subsection" or words of like import for organizational and
clarification purposes only. Such change to Village ordinances is not meant to
amend passage and effective dates of such original ordinances. (2018 Code)
1-3-2: GENERAL DEFINITIONS:
Whenever the following words or terms are used in this Code, they shall have
the meanings herein ascribed to them, unless the context makes such meaning
repugnant thereto:
CODE: The Village Code of the Village of Buckingham.
COUNTY: The County of Kankakee, State of Illinois.
ILCS: Illinois Compiled Statutes.
MAYOR: See definition of Village President.
PERSON: Any public or private corporation, firm, partnership, association,
organization, government or any other group acting as a unit, as well as a
natural person.
STATE: The State of Illinois.
VILLAGE: The Village of Buckingham, County of Kankakee, State of Illinois.
VILLAGE PRESIDENT: The President of the Village may be referred to as "Mayor"
or "President" of the Village. (2018 Code)
1-3-3: CATCHLINES:
The catchlines of the several sections of this Code are intended as mere
catchwords to indicate the content of the section and shall not be deemed or
taken to be titles of such sections, nor be deemed to govern, limit, modify or
in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of the provisions of any
section hereof, nor unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when
any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted. (2018
Code)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Application Of Provisions
1-4-3: Nonliability Of Officers And Employees
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY:
   A.   Any person convicted of a violation of any section or provision of this
Code, where no other penalty is set forth, shall be assessed a fine of one
hundred dollars ($100.00) per day per violation to a maximum of five hundred
dollars ($500.00) per day. The fine(s) shall be assessed on a daily basis until
such time as the violation(s) has been corrected. The Village shall be entitled
to collect any fees that are incurred in the prosecution of any violations of
this Code. This may include placing a lien on property, foreclosure of any lien
the Village may have thereon and any legal fees and costs. (Ord. 17-5, 8-8-
2017)
   B.   The provisions of subsection A of this section notwithstanding, no
penalty shall be greater than that established by State Statute for the same
offense. (2018 Code)
1-4-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Application Of Penalty: The penalty provided in this chapter shall be
applicable to every section of this Code the same as though it were a part of
each and every separate section unless otherwise indicated. Any person
convicted of a violation of any section of this Code where a duty is prescribed
or obligation imposed, or where any action which is of a continuing nature is
forbidden or is declared to be unlawful, shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor. A separate offense shall be deemed committed upon each day such
duty or obligation remains unperformed or such act continues, unless otherwise
specifically provided in this Code.
   B.   Acts Punishable Under Different Sections: In all cases where the same
offense is made punishable or is created by different clauses or sections of
this Code, the prosecuting officer may elect under which to proceed, but not
more than one recovery shall be had against the same person for the same
offense; provided, that the revocation of a license or permit shall not be
considered a recovery or penalty so as to bar any other penalty being enforced.
   C.   Breach Of Provisions: Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to
do any act constitutes a breach of any section or provision of this Code and
there shall be no fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the
provisions of this chapter shall apply. (2018 Code)
1-4-3: NONLIABILITY OF OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES:
No provision of this Code designating the duties of any officer or employee
shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee liable for any fine
or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty, unless the intent of
the Village Board of Trustees to impose such fine or penalty on such officer or
employee is specifically and clearly expressed in the section creating the
duty. (2018 Code)
CHAPTER 5
VILLAGE PRESIDENT
SECTION:
1-5-1: Election And Term
1-5-2: Oath And Bond
1-5-3: Powers And Duties
1-5-4: Appointment And Removal Of Village Officers
1-5-5: Vacancy In Office
1-5-6: President Pro Tem
1-5-1: ELECTION AND TERM:
The President of the Board of Trustees shall be elected for a four (4) year
term and shall serve until his successor is elected and qualified as is
provided by statute. (1987 Code §
1-5-1)
1-5-2: OATH AND BOND:
Before entering upon the duties of his office, the President of the Board of
Trustees shall subscribe to the required oath and shall execute a bond in such
amount and with such sureties as may be required by the Board of Trustees,
conditioned upon the faithful performance of the duties of his office. (1987
Code §
1-5-2)
1-5-3: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Generally: The President of the Board of Trustees shall be the Chief
Executive Officer of the Village and shall perform such duties as may be
required of him by statute or ordinance. He shall have supervision over all of
the executive officers and employees of the Village, except as by ordinance or
law shall be otherwise provided, and shall have the power and authority to
inspect all books and records pertaining to Village affairs and kept by any
officer or employee of the Village at any reasonable time. (1987 Code §
1-5-3)
   B.   Supervisory Duties:
      1.   Whenever there is a dispute as to the respective duties or powers of
any appointed officer of the Village, this dispute shall be settled by the
President of the Board of Trustees, after consultation with the Village
Attorney; and the President of the Board of Trustees shall have the power to
delegate to any appointed officer any duty which is to be performed when no
specific officer has been directed to perform that duty.
      2.   The President of the Board of Trustees shall supervise the conduct
of all officers of the Village and see that they faithfully and efficiently
discharge the duties of their respective offices. He shall inquire into all
reasonable complaints made against them and cause all their neglects or
violations of duty to be promptly corrected. He shall, in case he becomes
satisfied that any officer wilfully neglects or violates his duty, cause such
officer to be prosecuted and punished. (1987 Code §
1-5-5)
   C.   Signature: The President of the Board of Trustees shall sign all
commissions, licenses, permits and warrants granted, issued or drawn by order
of the Board of Trustees, or authorized by the ordinances of the Village. In
all contracts where the Village is a party, unless otherwise provided, the
President of the Board of Trustees shall sign the same on behalf of the
Village, and it shall be his special duty to see that the other contracting
party faithfully complies with the contract. (1987 Code §
1-5-6)
   D.   Suits Involving Village: In all suits wherein the Village is a party,
it shall be the duty of the President of the Board of Trustees to advise with
and assist the Village Attorney in prosecuting or defending the same, as the
case may be. (1987 Code § 1-5-7)
   E.   Village Representative: The President of the Board of Trustees shall
act for and on behalf of the Village on formal occasions and receptions; but in
his absence or inability to attend any such function, the Board of Trustees may
select any other Village officer to so act. (1987 Code § 1-5-8)
   F.   Additional Duties: In addition to the above and foregoing and to the
duties imposed upon him by law, the President shall perform all such other
duties as are or may be required of him by the ordinances of the Village. (1987
Code § 1-5-9)
1-5-4: APPOINTMENT AND REMOVAL OF VILLAGE OFFICERS:
   A.   Appointment: The Village President, upon, by and with the advice and
consent of the Board of Trustees, may appoint: 1) a Village Treasurer; 2) a
Village Clerk; 3) a Village Attorney; 4) a Building Inspector; 5) a Code
Enforcement Officer; and 6) such other officers as may be necessary to carry
into effect the powers conferred upon the Village by law and the ordinances of
the Village. (1987 Code §
1-5-4; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Removal From Office: Except where otherwise provided by statute, the
President of the Board of Trustees may remove any officer appointed by him on
any formal charge whenever he is of the opinion that the interests of the
Village demand removal, but he shall report the reasons of the removal to the
Board of Trustees at a meeting to be held not less than five (5) nor more than
ten (10) days after the removal. If the President of the Board of Trustees
fails or refuses to report to the Board of Trustees the reasons for the
removal, or if the Board of Trustees, by a two-thirds (2/3) vote of all its
members authorized by law to be elected, disapproves of the removal, the
officer thereupon shall be restored to the office from which he was removed.
The vote shall be by yeas and nays, which vote shall be entered upon the Board
of Trustees Journal. Upon restoration, the officer shall give a new bond and a
new oath of office. No officer shall be removed a second time for the same
offense. (1987 Code §
1-5-4)
1-5-5: VACANCY IN OFFICE:
Whenever a vacancy shall occur in the Office of President during his term, the
vacancy shall be filled for the remainder of the term as provided in 65
Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/3.1-10-50(f) or in the manner as otherwise
subsequently provided by the laws of the State of Illinois. During the period
from the time that the vacancy occurs until a President is elected, and has
qualified, the vacancy may be filled by the election of an Acting President by
the Board of Trustees. (1987 Code § 1-5-10; amd. 2018 Code)
1-5-6: PRESIDENT PRO TEM:
During a temporary absence or disability of the President of the Board of
Trustees, the Board of Trustees shall elect one of its members to act as
President Pro Tem who, during such absence or disability, shall possess the
powers of President of the Board of Trustees, as is provided by statute. (1987
Code § 1-5-11)
CHAPTER 6
VILLAGE BOARD OF TRUSTEES
SECTION:
1-6-1: Election And Term
1-6-2: Legislative Department Of Village
1-6-3: Oath And Compensation
1-6-4: Meetings
1-6-5: Rules And Order Of Business
1-6-6: Committees
1-6-7: Expenditures
1-6-1: ELECTION AND TERM:
The Board of Trustees, consisting of six (6) members, shall be elected to
office for four (4) year terms, according to the method provided by statute.
(1987 Code §
1-6-1)
1-6-2: LEGISLATIVE DEPARTMENT OF VILLAGE:
The Board shall be the Legislative Department of the Village government, and
shall perform such duties and have such powers as may be delegated by statute
thereto. (1987 Code §
1-6-2)
1-6-3: OATH AND COMPENSATION:
The members of the Board of Trustees shall take the oath of office prescribed
by statute, and shall receive such compensation as may be provided by
ordinance. (1987 Code §
1-6-3)
1-6-4: MEETINGS:
   A.   Regular Meetings: The Village Board shall hold its regular meetings in
the Village Hall on the first Tuesday of each month at seven o'clock (7:00)
P.M., and no notice of such regular meetings shall be required. The meeting
place of the said Board shall be at the Village Hall unless otherwise ordered
by the Board, except when said first Tuesday is a legal holiday, and under
those conditions, the following Tuesday shall be the regularly scheduled
meeting of the Board of Trustees. (Ord., 6-3-1997; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Adjourned Meetings: Adjourned meetings may be held for the purposes of
completing unfinished business of the regular meetings and such other purposes
as are necessary, at such time or times as may be determined by the President
and the Board of Trustees. (1987 Code §
1-6-4)
   C.   Special Meetings: Special meetings may be called by the President of
the Village or any three (3) Trustees upon at least forty eight (48) hours'
notice to all members and the President; provided, that if all of the Trustees
are present at a special meeting, no notice of the meeting shall be necessary,
and such notice shall be deemed waived.
   D.   Meetings Open To The Public: All meetings shall be open to the public
except for: 1) collective negotiating matters between the Village and its
employees; 2) meetings where a pending or prospective court proceeding against
or on behalf of the Village is being considered; 3) meetings to consider
information regarding appointment, employment or dismissal of an employee or
officer, or as provided by State law; provided, that no final action may be
taken at a closed session. (1987 Code §
1-6-4; amd. 2018 Code)
   E.   Presiding Officer: The President of the Board of Trustees shall be
presiding officer of the Board of Trustees at all regular and special meetings
and when the Board of Trustees meets as a Committee of the Whole. In the
absence of the President of the Board of Trustees, Acting President, or
President Pro Tem, the Board of Trustees may elect a Trustee to act as
Temporary Chair. He shall have only the powers of a presiding officer and a
right to vote in his capacity as Trustee on any ordinance, resolution or
motion. (1987 Code §
1-6-5)
   F.   Quorum: A majority of the President and the Trustees shall constitute a
quorum to do business, but no ordinance shall be passed except upon the
favorable vote of a majority of the elected members, as provided by statute.
(1987 Code §
1-6-6)
1-6-5: RULES AND ORDER OF BUSINESS:
   A.   Order Of Business: The order of business of the Village Board of
Trustees shall be as follows: (1987 Code §
1-6-7)
      1.   Call to order.
      2.   Roll call.
      3.   Minutes.
      4.   Treasurer's report.
      5.   Bills.
      6.   Committee reports:
   Building and Grounds.
   Health and Welfare.
   Planning and Zoning.
   Police.
   Streets and Alleys.
   Water and Sewer.
      7.   Correspondence.
      8.   Unfinished business.
      9.   Executive session.
      10.   New business.
      11.   Adjournment. (1987 Code §
1-6-7; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Duties Of President: The President of the Board of Trustees shall
preserve order and decorum, and shall decide all questions of order, subject to
an appeal to the Board of Trustees. Appeals to the Board of Trustees shall be
decided without debate, and the decision of the President shall prevail, unless
reversed by a two-thirds (2/3) adverse vote of the Trustees present.
   C.   Rescinded Action: No vote or action of the Board of Trustees shall be
rescinded at any special meeting of the Board of Trustees unless there be
present at such special meeting as many members of the Board of Trustees as
were present at the meeting when such vote or action was taken, as provided by
statute.
   D.   Resolutions: Any resolutions submitted to the Board of Trustees shall
be reduced to writing before being voted upon on request of any two (2) members
of the Board.
   E.   Addressing Meetings: No person other than the President or a member of
the Board shall address that body at any regular or special meeting, except
upon consent of a majority of the members present.
   F.   Speaking Restricted:
      1.   No person other than the President and members of the Board of
Trustees shall be allowed to speak before the Board of Trustees, except by
permission given by the Board.
      2.   No member shall speak more than twice upon any question, nor more
than ten (10) minutes at one time, except by permission of the Board of
Trustees.
   G.   Communications To Be In Writing: All petitions and other communications
to the Board of Trustees shall be in writing.
   H.   Committee Reports, Documents Required: Every committee of the Board of
Trustees in reporting upon any subject referred to them, shall attach to their
report all papers and documents in the possession of the committee relative to
the matter so referred when so requested by a majority of the Board.
   I.   Voting Restricted: No member shall vote on any matter in which he is
directly interested, but all members shall vote upon all other questions unless
excused by the Board of Trustees.
   J.   Motion To Adjourn: A motion to adjourn shall always be in order, and
shall be decided without debate. (1987 Code §
1-6-7)
   K.   Disturbing Meetings: It shall be unlawful to disturb any regular or
special meeting of the Board of Trustees or of any committee thereof, or to
behave in a disorderly manner at any such meeting. Any person violating any
provision of this subsection shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this title for each offense. (1987 Code §
1-6-7; amd. 2018 Code)
   L.   Rules Of Order:
      1.   Robert's Rules Of Order: Robert's Rules of Order shall govern the
deliberations of the Board of Trustees except when in conflict with any of the
foregoing rules.
      2.   Adoption Of Rules Of Order: The President and Board of Trustees may
from time to time adopt by resolution, rules of order for their guidance and
control, which rules shall be enforced until repealed, altered or amended,
unless by concurrence of two-thirds (2/3) of all the members elected, they
shall be suspended for that meeting.
      3.   Suspension Of Rules Of Order: The rules of order, other than those
prescribed by statute, may be suspended at any time by the consent of a
majority of the members present at any meeting. (1987 Code §
1-6-7)
1-6-6: COMMITTEES:
   A.   Standing Committees: The following shall be the standing committees of
the Board of Trustees:
Committee on Building and Grounds.
Committee on Health and Welfare.
Committee on Liquor Control (the President is the Liquor Control Commissioner).
Committee on Planning and Zoning.
Committee on Police.
Committee on Streets and Alleys.
Committee on Water and Sewer. (1987 Code § 1-6-8; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Special Committees: The President of the Board of Trustees shall
appoint such special committees as he may deem necessary or as may be directed
by the Board of Trustees. (1987 Code § 1-6-9)
1-6-7: EXPENDITURES:
No committee of the Village Board, nor any member of said Board or other
officer of the Village, shall expend or contract for the expenditure of any
monies belonging to the Village, or incur liability on the part of the Village,
without the prior authority of the Village Board to so do, or unless authorized
so to do by ordinance or resolution of the Village Board. (1987 Code § 1-6-10)
CHAPTER 7
VILLAGE OFFICERS AND PERSONNEL
SECTION:
1-7-1: Qualifications For Elective Office
1-7-2: Terms Of Office
1-7-3: Oath Of Office
1-7-4: Bonds
1-7-5: Compensation
1-7-6: Conflict Of Interest
1-7-7: Office Exclusive
1-7-8: Sexual Harassment Policy Adopted
1-7-1: QUALIFICATIONS FOR ELECTIVE OFFICE:
   A.   No person shall be eligible to any elective office in the Village who
is not a qualified elector of the Village and who shall not have resided
therein at least one year next preceding the election nor shall any person be
eligible to any office, elective or appointive, who is a defaulter to the
Village.
   B.   If the President or any other elected Village official shall, during
his official term, remove his residence beyond the limits of the Village, his
office shall thereby become vacant. (1987 Code §
1-7-1)
1-7-2: TERMS OF OFFICE:
   A.   Elective Officers: All elective officers shall hold office for a term
of four (4) years, unless by ordinance or statute it is otherwise provided, or
unless elected to fill a vacancy. The terms of all elective officers shall
commence immediately following the adjournment of the first regular or special
meeting of the Board of Trustees following the proclamation of the results of
the election, unless otherwise required by law.
   B.   Elected Officers To Fill Vacancies: The terms of all officers elected
to fill a vacancy shall commence immediately upon the qualification of such
elected officer for such office in accordance with the law.
   C.   Appointive Officers And Employees: The terms of all appointive officers
and employees shall commence upon appointment and qualification for said office
as provided by law, which appointment shall be for a period of time until a
successor for said appointee is duly appointed and qualified. (1987 Code §
1-7-2)
1-7-3: OATH OF OFFICE:
   A.   All of the elected and appointed officers of the Village shall, before
entering upon the duties of their respective offices, take and subscribe the
following oath or affirmation:
I do solemnly swear (or affirm) that I will support the Constitution of the
United States, and the Constitution of the State of Illinois; that I will
faithfully discharge the duties of the office of (here insert the name of the
office to which he is elected or appointed) according to the best of my
ability.
   B.   The said oath or affirmation so subscribed, shall be filed in the
Office of the Village Clerk, except that of the Village Clerk, which shall be
filed with the Village Treasurer. (1987 Code §
1-7-3)
1-7-4: BONDS:
   A.   Generally: Before entering upon the duties of their respective offices,
all Village officers, except members of the Board of Trustees, shall execute a
bond with security to be approved by the Board of Trustees as provided by law
or ordinances of the Village. These bonds shall be filed with the Village
Clerk, except the bond of the Clerk, which shall be filed with the Village
Treasurer.
   B.   Village President: The Village President shall, before entering upon
the duties of his office after his appointment or election, execute a bond with
security, to be approved by the Board of Trustees payable to the Village in the
penal sum of ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00), conditioned upon his faithful
performance of the duties of the Office of President and the payment of all
monies received by him as Village President and the delivery to his successor
in office of all property, books and effects in his possession belonging to the
Village or pertaining to the Office of Village President according to law and
the ordinances of the Village.
   C.   Village Clerk: The Village Clerk shall, before entering upon the duties
of his office after his appointment or election, execute a bond with security,
to be approved by the Board of Trustees, payable to the Village in the penal
sum of ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00), conditioned upon the faithful
performance of the duties of the Office of Village Clerk, payment of all monies
received as Village Clerk and the delivery to his successor in office of all
property, books and effects in his possession belonging to the Village or
appertaining to the Office of Village Clerk according to law and the ordinances
of the Village.
   D.   Village Treasurer: The Village Treasurer shall, before he enters upon
the duties of his office after his appointment, execute and deliver to the
Village Clerk a bond to be approved by the Board of Trustees with at least two
(2) good and sufficient securities in a sum that is not less than three (3)
times the latest Federal census population or any subsequent census figure used
for Motor Fuel Tax purposes, conditioned upon the faithful performance of the
duties of his Office of Village Treasurer and the payment of and accounting for
monies received as Treasurer according to law and ordinances. (1987 Code §
1-7-4; amd. 2018 Code)
1-7-5: COMPENSATION:
   A.   Salaries:
      1.   Village President: The salary of the President is hereby fixed at
the sum of seventy five dollars ($75.00) per meeting or per diem. This salary
increase is effective May 1, 2015.
      2.   Village Trustees: Each Trustee shall receive for his/her service
thirty seven dollars fifty cents ($37.50) per meeting or per diem. This salary
increase is effective May 1, 2015.
      3.   Village Clerk: The salary of the Village Clerk is hereby fixed at
two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) per month. The Clerk shall receive no other
compensation. This salary increase is effective May 1, 2014. (Ord. 14-1, 5-6-
2014)
      4.   Village Treasurer: The salary of the Village Treasurer is hereby
fixed at the sum of three hundred twenty five dollars ($325.00) per month. The
Treasurer shall receive no other compensation. This salary increase is
effective May 1, 2014. (Ord. 14-1, 5-6-2014; amd. 2018 Code)
      5.   Village Attorney: The salary of the Village Attorney shall be in the
amount as approved by the President and Board of Trustees at the time of
appointment. (1987 Code §
1-7-5)
      6.   Village Water Pumper: The salary of the water pumper is hereby fixed
at two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) per month. This salary increase is
effective May 1, 2014. (Ord. 14-1, 5-6-2014; amd. 2018 Code)
      7.   Temporary Suspension Of Services: Nothing in this Code shall create
an absolute right in any official or employee to receive his or her entire
annual salary, or other compensation, where it is necessary on the part of the
Board to make a temporary suspension of the services of one or more officials
or employees because of the lack of Village funds with which to pay for the
suspended services.
   B.   Per Diem Determination: For purposes of determining payments on a per
diem basis, whenever the President or Trustees are required to act in their
official capacity, they shall submit a voucher requesting a per diem payment
for such services performed.
   C.   Mileage Reimbursement: Each officer and employee of the Village shall
be reimbursed for mileage arising from the use of their personal vehicle. The
rate of reimbursement shall be set on a regular basis by the Board of Trustees.
(1987 Code §
1-7-5)
   D.   Determining Payment For President And Trustees: The President and
Trustees will be paid on a bi-yearly schedule as follows: Anyone on the Village
Board will be able to miss no more than three (3) meetings in a year and no
more than two (2) meetings in a six (6) month period. If this criteria is met,
then the President or Trustee will receive his/her full six (6) month salary.
If for any reason the President or Trustee fails to meet the criteria, then
after missing the numbered meetings, the single monthly salary will be
subtracted from the six (6) month salary for every month missed. (2018 Code)
1-7-6: CONFLICT OF INTEREST:
No member of the Village Board or other Village officer shall be interested,
either directly or indirectly, in any contract with or work for the Village, or
become surety for any contractor or other person upon any bond to secure the
performance of any contract with the Village. (1987 Code §
1-7-6)
1-7-7: OFFICE EXCLUSIVE:
No President, Trustee, Village Clerk or Village Treasurer shall hold any other
office under the Village government during his term of office. (1987 Code §
1-7-7)
1-7-8: SEXUAL HARASSMENT POLICY ADOPTED:
The "Policy Prohibiting Sexual Harassment", included as exhibit A on file in
the Village, is hereby adopted. Copies of said policy are on file in the Office
of the Village Clerk for public use and inspection. (Ord. 17-9, 12-5-2017, eff.
12-5-2017; amd. 2018 Code)
ARTICLE A. VILLAGE CLERK
SECTION:
1-7A-1: Appointment And Term
1-7A-2: Oath And Bond
1-7A-3: Duties
1-7A-4: Deputy Clerk
1-7A-1: APPOINTMENT AND TERM:
The Village Clerk shall be appointed by the Village President, by and with the
advice and consent of the Village Board, and shall serve until his successor is
selected and qualified according to law. (1987 Code §
1-7A-1; amd. 2018 Code)
1-7A-2: OATH AND BOND:
Before entering upon the duties of his office, the Village Clerk shall
subscribe to the required oath and shall execute a bond in such amount and with
such sureties as may be required by the Board of Trustees, conditioned upon the
faithful performance of his duties. (1987 Code §
1-7A-2)
1-7A-3: DUTIES:
The Village Clerk shall:
   A.   Seal and attest all contracts of the Village, and all licenses, permits
and other such documents as shall require this formality.
   B.   Turn over all monies received by him on behalf of the Village to the
Village Treasurer promptly, on receipt of the same; and with such monies he
shall give a statement as to the source thereof.
   C.   Keep accounts showing all monies received by him, and the source and
disposition thereof, and such other accounts as may be required by statute or
ordinance.
   D.   In addition to the records of ordinances and other records which the
Clerk is required by statute to keep, keep a register of all licenses and
permits issued and the payments thereon, a record showing all of the officers
and regular employees of the Village, and such other records as may be required
by the Board of Trustees.
   E.   Be the custodian of the Village Seal, and shall affix its impression on
documents whenever this is required.
   F.   Be the custodian of all documents belonging to the Village which are
not assigned to the custody of some other officer of the Village by the
President or Board of Trustees.
   G.   Keep and maintain a proper index to all documents and records kept by
him so that ready access thereto and use thereof may be had.
   H.   Keep a record of the election or appointment and confirmation of all
officers of the Village, and said record shall be so ruled and headed that the
same shall exhibit the name of the officer elected or appointed, the date of
confirmation or election, the date of commission and the date of deaths,
resignation or removal or expiration of term of office with a column for
remarks.
   I.   Not allow any books, records or papers or other instruments of writing
to be taken out of his office by any person other than himself, the President,
any of the Board of Trustees and the Village Attorney, or upon the order of a
court of competent jurisdiction or the Board of Trustees.
   J.   Attend all meetings of the President and Board of Trustees and keep in
a suitable book for the purpose a full and faithful record of its proceedings.
He shall issue and cause to be served upon the President and Board of Trustees
notice of all special meetings of the President and Board of Trustees.
   K.   In a separate book, keep a record of all ordinances passed by the
President and Board of Trustees, and if the ordinance requires posting or
publication, he shall cause the same to be duly posted or published.
   L.   In addition to the duties herein provided, perform such other duties
and functions as may be required by statute or ordinance. (1987 Code §
1-7A-3)
1-7A-4: DEPUTY CLERK:
The Village Clerk may, subject to the approval of the President, appoint any
adult resident of the Village as his deputy for the purpose of the issuance of
licenses and permits or attending meetings of the Board of Trustees and acting
as Clerk when the Clerk is temporarily absent from the Village. (1987 Code §
1-7A-4)
ARTICLE B. VILLAGE TREASURER
SECTION:
1-7B-1: Appointment And Term
1-7B-2: Duties
1-7B-3: Funds Separate
1-7B-1: APPOINTMENT AND TERM:
The Village Treasurer shall be appointed at the commencement of the fiscal year
by the President, with the approval of the Board of Trustees, and shall serve
until his successor is qualified as is provided by law. (1987 Code §
1-7B-1)
1-7B-2: DUTIES:
The Treasurer shall:
   A.   Perform such duties as may be prescribed for him by statute or by
ordinance.
   B.   Receive all monies paid to the Village and belonging to the Village,
either directly from the person paying it or from the hands of such other
officer as may receive it and shall keep a separate account of each fund and
appropriation.
   C.   Pay out money only on vouchers or orders properly signed by the Village
Clerk and the President of the Board of Trustees.
   D.   Keep true and complete accounts and records, fully itemized, of all
warrants redeemed and paid by him, but he shall pay out no money except on
warrants therefor, signed by the President and countersigned by the Clerk,
stating the particular fund or appropriation to which the same is chargeable,
and the person to whom payable. No money shall be otherwise paid out than upon
such warrants so drawn.
   E.   Keep a register of all warrants, bonds or orders filed with him or paid
by him, and all vouchers, as is required by statute.
   F.   Deposit the Village funds in such depositories as may be selected from
time to time as is provided by law.
   G.   Keep true and correct records showing all monies received by him, the
source from which it was received and the purpose for which it was paid out;
and he shall keep a record showing at all times the financial status of the
Village.
   H.   Keep such books and accounts as may be required by the Board of
Trustees, and shall keep them in the manner required by the Board of Trustees.
Said books and accounts shall always be subject to the inspection of any member
of the Board of Trustees.
   I.   Render to the Board of Trustees a verified report, at the first regular
meeting of the Board of Trustees in each month or more often if required, of
all his transactions the preceding month. He shall also annually, within thirty
(30) days after the close of the fiscal year, make out and file with the Clerk
a full and detailed account of all such receipts and expenditures and of all
his transactions as such Treasurer during the preceding fiscal year, and shall
show in such account the state of the Treasury at the close of the fiscal year;
which account the Clerk shall immediately either cause to be published in a
newspaper having a general circulation in the Village, or by posting the same
in a public place in the Clerk's Office.
   J.   Report to the Village Clerk any officer authorized to receive money for
the use of the Village who may fail to make a return of the monies received by
him at the time required by law, or by the ordinances of the Village.
   K.   In addition to the foregoing duties, perform all such other and further
duties pertaining to his office as are or may be imposed upon him by law or
ordinance. (1987 Code §
1-7B-2)
1-7B-3: FUNDS SEPARATE:
The Treasurer shall keep the Village money separate and distinct from his own
and shall not intermingle his own money therewith or make private or personal
use of the Village funds. (1987 Code §
1-7B-3)
ARTICLE C. CODE ENFORCEMENT OFFICER
SECTION:
1-7C-1: Office Created; Appointment
1-7C-2: Duties
1-7C-3: Compensation
1-7C-1: OFFICE CREATED; APPOINTMENT:
The Office of Code Enforcement Officer is hereby created, who shall be
appointed by the Village President, with the consent of the Board of Trustees.
(Ord. 12-4, 2-6-2012)
1-7C-2: DUTIES:
It shall be the duty of the Code Enforcement Officer to enforce Property
Maintenance Codes, ordinances and other regulations governing the condition and
maintenance of all property, buildings and structures and supplied utilities
and facilities and other physical things and conditions essential to ensure
that structures are safe and sanitary and fit for occupation and use. The Code
Enforcement Officer shall make inspections, as deemed necessary, issue all
necessary notices or orders, and keep official records pertaining to
inspections, notices, orders and fees collected. (Ord. 12-4, 2-6-2012)
1-7C-3: COMPENSATION:
The compensation of the Code Enforcement Officer shall be determined by the
Board of Trustees. (Ord. 12-4, 2-6-2012)
CHAPTER 8
ETHICS
SECTION:
1-8-1: State Regulations Adopted
1-8-2: Definitions
1-8-3: Interpretation
1-8-4: Prohibited Acts
1-8-5: Penalties
1-8-6: Amendments
1-8-7: Unconstitutionality Of Provisions
1-8-1: STATE REGULATIONS ADOPTED:
The regulations of 5 Illinois Compiled Statutes 430/5-15 and 5 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 430/10-10 through 430/10-40 of the State Officials and
Employees Ethics Act, 5 Illinois Compiled Statutes 430/1-1 et seq. (hereinafter
referred to as the "Act" in this chapter), are hereby adopted by reference and
made applicable to the officers and employees of the Village to the extent
required by 5 Illinois Compiled Statutes 430/70-5. (2018 Code)
1-8-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the terms "officer" and "employee" shall be
defined as set forth in 5 Illinois Compiled Statutes 430/70-5(c). (2018 Code)
1-8-3: INTERPRETATION:
This chapter does not repeal or otherwise amend or modify any existing
ordinances or policies which regulate the conduct of Village officers and
employees. To the extent that any such existing ordinances or policies are less
restrictive than this chapter, however, the provisions of this chapter shall
prevail in accordance with the provisions of 5 Illinois Compiled Statutes 430/
70-5(a). (2018 Code)
1-8-4: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   Gifts:
      1.   The solicitation or acceptance of gifts prohibited to be solicited
or accepted under the Act by any officer or any employee of the Village is
hereby prohibited.
      2.   The offering or making of gifts prohibited to be offered or made to
an officer or employee of the Village under the Act is hereby prohibited.
   B.   Political Activities: The participation in political activities
prohibited under the Act by any officer or employee of the Village is hereby
prohibited. (2018 Code)
1-8-5: PENALTIES:
The penalties for violations of this chapter shall be the same as those
penalties set forth in 5 Illinois Compiled Statutes 430/50-5 for similar
violations of the Act. (2018 Code)
1-8-6: AMENDMENTS:
Any amendment to the Act that becomes effective after the effective date hereof
shall be incorporated into this chapter by reference and shall be applicable to
the solicitation, acceptance, offering and making of gifts and to prohibited
political activities. However, any amendment that makes its provisions optional
for adoption by the Village shall not be incorporated into this chapter by
reference without formal action by the Corporate Authorities of the Village.
(2018 Code)
1-8-7: UNCONSTITUTIONALITY OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   If the Illinois Supreme Court declares the Act unconstitutional in its
entirety, then this chapter shall be repealed as of the date that the Illinois
Supreme Court's decision becomes final and not subject to any further appeals
or rehearings. This chapter shall be deemed repealed without further action by
the Corporate Authorities of the Village if the Act is found unconstitutional
by the Illinois Supreme Court.
   B.   If the Illinois Supreme Court declares part of the Act unconstitutional
but upholds the constitutionality of the remainder of the Act, or does not
address the remainder of the Act, then the remainder of the Act, as adopted by
this chapter, shall remain in full force and effect; however, that part of this
chapter relating to the part of the Act found unconstitutional shall be deemed
repealed without further action by the Corporate Authorities of the Village.
(2018 Code)
CHAPTER 9
PUBLIC RECORDS ACCESS
SECTION:
1-9-1: Request Of Records From Clerk
1-9-2: Retrieval Of Records
1-9-3: Fees
1-9-4: Appeal Of Request Denial
1-9-5: Directories, Subdivision Diagram And Records Catalogue
1-9-1: REQUEST OF RECORDS FROM CLERK:
The Village Clerk is hereby designated as the person to whom all initial
requests for access to the records of the Village are to be referred. Any
person requesting records of the Village may make such a request in person or
in writing at the Village Clerk's Office located at 1 North Willow. Such
request should be made in person. Another method would be by mailing the
request to the Village Clerk specifying in particular the records requested to
be disclosed and copied. All written requests should be addressed to the
Village Clerk, PO Box 65, Buckingham, IL 60917. (Ord., 2-18-1996; amd. 2018
Code)
1-9-2: RETRIEVAL OF RECORDS:
Any records which are the subject of a request under the Freedom of Information
Act shall be retrieved from such place as they are stored, by the Village
Clerk. In no event shall records be retrieved by the party requesting them or
by any person who is not employed by the Village. (Ord., 2-18-1996)
1-9-3: FEES:
The fees for any records, if the person requesting the records wishes them to
be copied, are as follows:
   A.   Fifteen cents ($0.15) per page.
   B.   If it is an FOIA request, the first fifty (50) pages are free, then
pages fifty one plus (51+) will be at the fee of fifteen cents ($0.15) per
page.
   C.   If certified copies are requested, there will be an extra ten cents
($0.10) per page charged. (2018 Code)
1-9-4: APPEAL OF REQUEST DENIAL:
In the event that a request to inspect Village records is denied by the Village
Clerk, the denial may be appealed to the Village President. Such an appeal must
be made within fourteen (14) days after the requesting party receives written
notice denying said request; or in the event that the denial is not by letter,
the appeal must be made fourteen (14) days after the request is effectively
denied. In the absence of the Village President, appeals from denials of
requests for access shall be made to the Board of Trustees. (Ord., 2-18-1996)
1-9-5: DIRECTORIES, SUBDIVISION DIAGRAM AND RECORDS CATALOGUE:
The Village Clerk shall prepare: a) a Village information directory; b) a block
diagram of the functional subdivisions of the Village; c) a Village records
directory; and d) a records catalogue, all of which shall be substantially in
the same form as the documents attached and made a part hereof as exhibits A,
B, C, and D on file in the Village. (Ord., 2-18-1996)
CHAPTER 10
ELECTIONS
SECTION:
1-10-1: Voting Qualifications
1-10-1: VOTING QUALIFICATIONS:
All persons who are entitled to vote at any general election for State officers
and who have a permanent abode within the Municipality may vote therein at any
election for Municipal officers or at any election on Municipal bond issues or
propositions. (1987 Code §
1-9-1)
TITLE 2
BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-1-1: Commission Established; Membership; Terms; Chair; Removals And
Vacancies; Meetings
2-1-2: Duties
2-1-3: Compensation
2-1-1: COMMISSION ESTABLISHED; MEMBERSHIP; TERMS; CHAIR; REMOVALS AND
VACANCIES; MEETINGS:
A Planning Commission is hereby authorized to be established. The Planning
Commission shall consist of three (3) members appointed by the Village
President, with the consent of the Board of Trustees. The members of the
Planning Commission shall serve respectively for the following terms, or until
their respective successors are appointed and qualified: one for one year; one
for two (2) years; and one for three (3) years. The successor to each member so
appointed will serve for a term of three (3) years. One of the members of the
Planning Commission shall be designated by the Village President, with the
consent of the Board of Trustees, as Chair of the Planning Commission, and
shall hold his said office as Chair until his successor is appointed. Such
Chair, or in his absence the Acting Chair, may administer oaths and compel the
attendance of witnesses. The Village President shall have the power to remove
any member of the Planning Commission for cause and after a public hearing.
Vacancies upon the Planning Commission shall be filled for the unexpired term
of the member whose place has become vacant in the manner herein provided for
the appointment of such member. The meetings of the Planning Commission shall
be held at such times as the Planning Commission, by rule, directs. (1987 Code
§
2-1-1)
2-1-2: DUTIES:
The Planning Commission is to recommend the boundaries of various districts and
appropriate regulations to be enforced therein and to study the zoning and
planning needs of the Village, give notice, hold hearings, formulate
comprehensive zoning and to carry on these same functions relative to the
rezoning districts or amendments of the subdivision regulations or zoning title
of this Code. (1987 Code §
2-1-2)
2-1-3: COMPENSATION:
Each member of the Planning Commission shall receive the sum of fifteen dollars
($15.00) per meeting as his compensation for his attendance to each meeting of
said Planning Commission, payable at the end of each fiscal year. (1987 Code §
2-1-3)
TITLE 3
VILLAGE FINANCES
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL FINANCE PROVISIONS
SECTION:
3-1-1: Municipal Or Fiscal Year
3-1-2: Annual Appropriation Ordinance
3-1-3: Annual Tax Levy Ordinance
3-1-4: Annual Audit
3-1-5: Expenditures; Payment Of Bills
3-1-6: Annual Department Inventory
3-1-1: MUNICIPAL OR FISCAL YEAR:
The Municipal or fiscal year of the Village shall commence on May 1 in each
year. (1987 Code §
1-8-1)
3-1-2: ANNUAL APPROPRIATION ORDINANCE:
The President and the Board of Trustees shall, as soon as practicable after the
commencement of each fiscal year, and within the first quarter thereof, pass an
ordinance to be termed the annual appropriation ordinance, in which they shall
appropriate such sums of money as may be deemed necessary to defray all
necessary expenses and liabilities of the Village government during the fiscal
year, and in such ordinance shall specify the different objects and purposes
for which such appropriations are made, and the amount appropriated for each
object or purpose, and no further appropriations shall be made at any time
during the fiscal year, except as otherwise expressly provided by law. (1987
Code §
1-8-2)
3-1-3: ANNUAL TAX LEVY ORDINANCE:
The President and Board of Trustees shall annually, on or before the third
Tuesday in September in each year, ascertain the total amount of appropriations
for all corporate purposes legally made and to be collected from the tax levy
of that fiscal year; and by an ordinance specifying in detail the purpose for
which such appropriations are made, and the sum or amount appropriated for each
purpose respectively, levy the amount so ascertained upon all the property
subject to taxation within the Village as the same is assessed and equalized
for State and County purposes for the current year, a copy of which ordinance
shall be filed with the County Clerk by the Village Clerk. (1987 Code §
1-8-3)
3-1-4: ANNUAL AUDIT:
The records and accounts of the Village shall be fully audited to the end of
each fiscal year by some impartial accountant selected by the Board of Trustees
for that purpose, which audit shall be made in accordance with the Illinois
Municipal Auditing Law. (1987 Code §
1-8-4)
3-1-5: EXPENDITURES; PAYMENT OF BILLS:
No bills, claims or expenditures of any kind or nature shall be paid and no
order drawn on the Village Treasurer therefor, unless such bills or claims
shall have been regularly passed on and allowed by the Village Board,
specifying upon what fund the order shall be drawn; except, that the Treasurer
is hereby authorized to pay standard and customary utility bills if it is
necessary to pay said bills before the next regularly scheduled meeting in
order to avoid late charges. (1987 Code §
1-8-5)
3-1-6: ANNUAL DEPARTMENT INVENTORY:
Each officer and head of each committee shall, annually, on May 1 of each year,
submit to the Board an inventory of the equipment, supplies, materials and
invoices on hand. (1987 Code §
1-8-6)
CHAPTER 2
INVESTMENT POLICY; VILLAGE DEPOSITORIES
SECTION:
3-2-1: Scope
3-2-2: General Objectives
3-2-3: Standard Of Care
3-2-1: SCOPE:
This policy applies to the investment of all operating and investment funds.
Except for funds which by law must be segregated, funds may be pooled for
convenience and to maximize investment earnings. Funds that are pooled shall be
separated in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles. (Ord.
99-7, 12-13-1999)
3-2-2: GENERAL OBJECTIVES:
The primary objectives, in priority order, of investment activities shall be
safety, liquidity and yield.
   A.   Safety: Safety of principal is the foremost objective of the investment
policy. Investments shall be undertaken in a manner that seeks to ensure the
preservation of capital. The objective will be to mitigate credit risk and
interest rate risk.
      1.   Risk To Principal: The Village will minimize risk to loss of
principal assets by:
         a.   Limiting investments to the safest types of securities;
         b.   Prequalifying the financial institutions, broker/dealers,
intermediaries, and advisors with which an entity will do business; and
         c.   Diversifying the investment portfolio so that potential losses on
individual securities will be minimized.
      2.   Interest Rate Risk: The Village will minimize the risk that the
market value of securities in the portfolio will fall due to changes in general
interest rate by:
         a.   Structuring the investment portfolio so that securities meet cash
requirements for ongoing operations.
         b.   Investing operating funds primarily in instruments with
determined interest rates.
   B.   Liquidity: The investment portfolio shall bear interest payments
sufficiently to meet all operating requirements that may be reasonably
anticipated. This is accomplished by structuring the portfolio so that
securities bear interest or mature concurrent with cash needs to meet
anticipated financial demands of the district. Furthermore, since all possible
cash demands cannot be anticipated, the investment portfolio shall contain some
liquid investments.
   C.   Yield: The investment portfolio shall be designed with the objective of
attaining a near to market rate of return with the preference of using local
banks for investment purposes. Return on investment is of secondary importance
compared to the safety and need for established interest income rates as
described above. (Ord. 99-7, 12-13-1999)
3-2-3: STANDARD OF CARE:
   A.   Prudence:
      1.   The standard of prudence to be used by investment officials shall be
the "prudent person" standard and shall be applied in the context of managing
an overall portfolio. Investment officers acting in accordance with written
procedures and this investment policy and exercising due diligence shall be
relieved of personal responsibility for an individual security's credit risk or
market price changes, provided deviations from expectations are reported in a
timely fashion and the liquidity and the sale of securities are carried out in
accordance with the terms of this policy.
      2.   Investments shall be made with judgment and care, under
circumstances then prevailing, which persons of prudence, discretion and
intelligence exercise in the management of their own affairs, not for
speculation, but for investment, considering the probable safety of their
capital as well as the probable income to be derived.
   B.   Ethics And Conflicts Of Interest: Officers and employees involved in
the investment process shall refrain from personal business activity that could
conflict with proper execution and management of the investment program, or
that could impair their ability to make impartial decisions. Employees and
investment officials shall disclose any material interests in financial
institutions with which they conduct business. They shall further disclose any
personal financial/investment positions that could be related to the
performance of the investment portfolio. Employees and officers shall refrain
from undertaking personal investment transactions with the same individual with
whom business is conducted on behalf of the district.
   C.   Delegation Of Authority:
      1.   Authority to manage the investment program is granted to the Village
Treasurer, hereinafter referred to as the "investment officer".
      2.   Responsibility for the operation of the investment policy is hereby
delegated to the investment officer, who shall act in accordance with this
investment policy keeping the District's Treasurer advised of all financial
transactions and following the below internal controls to protect from loss,
theft or misuse:
         a.   All transactions shall bear the signature of the Treasurer. Any
transactions over ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00) should bear the signature
of the Treasurer and the Village President. A Village Trustee shall sign in
absence of the Treasurer or Village President.
         b.   Investment transactions shall be handled in person when
practical.
         c.   Records of all financial transactions shall be made within forty
eight (48) hours of such transactions.
         d.   The Treasurer shall present a financial report at every meeting
and at least quarterly provide a written report of investment activities. The
Treasurer shall have present at all meetings the most current statements
verifying account balances should the Board desire to audit any accounts.
         e.   Accounts at any one financial institution shall not exceed FDIC
limits unless further security is provided as required by Illinois law.
         f.   As a further internal control, the investment officer shall
review records with a CPA for an annual independent review to assure compliance
with sound policies and procedures. The internal controls shall review:
            (1)   Control of collusion.
            (2)   Separation of transaction authority from accounting and
recordkeeping.
            (3)   Custodial safekeeping.
            (4)   Avoidance of physical-delivery securities.
            (5)   Clear delegation of authority to subordinate staff members.
            (6)   Written confirmation of telephone transactions for
investments and wire transfers.
            (7)   Development of a wire transfer agreement with the lead bank
or third party custodian.
   D.   Authorized Financial Institutions:
      1.   The following are approved financial institutions authorized to
provide investment services: State Bank of Herscher, Illinois Public
Treasurer's Investment Pool.
      2.   This list of approved financial institutions shall be annually
reviewed and may be amended by Board resolution. Financial institutions who
desire to become qualified bidders for investment transactions must supply the
following as appropriate:
         a.   Audited financial statements.
         b.   Proof of National Association of Securities Dealers (NASD)
certification.
         c.   Proof of State registration.
         d.   Completed broker/dealer questionnaire.
         e.   Certification of having read the entity's investment policy.
(Ord. 99-7, 12-13-1999)
TITLE 4
BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL LICENSING AND PERMIT PROVISIONS
SECTION:
4-1-1: Application For License Or Permit
4-1-2: Forms
4-1-3: Signatures Required
4-1-4: Inspections Or Investigations
4-1-5: Fees And Charges
4-1-6: Term Of License
4-1-7: Posting License
4-1-8: Nontransferability Of License; Change Of Location
4-1-9: Building And Premises
4-1-10: Nuisance Businesses Prohibited
4-1-11: Authority To Grant Licenses; Suspension Or Revocation Of Licenses
4-1-11-1: Suspension Of License
4-1-11-2: Notice Of License Denial Or Revocation
4-1-11-3: Hearings On License Denial Or Revocation
4-1-12: Penalty
4-1-1: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE OR PERMIT:
Applications for all licenses and permits required by ordinance shall be made
in writing to the Village Clerk, in the absence of any other provision to the
contrary. Each application shall state the name of the applicant, the permit or
license desired, the location to be used, if any, the time covered and the fee
to be paid; and each application shall contain such additional information as
may be needed for the proper guidance of the Village officials in the issuing
of the said permit or license. (1987 Code §
3-1-1)
4-1-2: FORMS:
Forms for all licenses and permits, and applications therefor, shall be
prepared and kept on hand by the Village Clerk. (1987 Code §
3-1-2)
4-1-3: SIGNATURES REQUIRED:
Each license or permit issued shall bear the signatures of the President and
the Clerk, in the absence of any provision to the contrary. (1987 Code §
3-1-3)
4-1-4: INSPECTIONS OR INVESTIGATIONS:
Upon receipt of an application for a license or permit where the ordinances of
the Village require an inspection or investigation before the issuance of such
permit or license, the Village Clerk shall refer such application to the proper
official or officials for making such investigation within forty eight (48)
hours of the time of such receipt. The official charged with the duty of making
the investigation or inspection shall make a report thereon, favorable or
otherwise, within ten (10) days after receiving the application or a copy
thereof. (1987 Code §
3-1-5)
4-1-5: FEES AND CHARGES:
   A.   Payment In Advance: In the absence of any provision to the contrary,
all fees and charges for licenses or permits shall be paid in advance at the
time the application therefor is made to the Village Clerk.
   B.   Proration Of Fee: When an application for an annual license is made
after the expiration of six (6) months of the current license year, the license
for the remainder of the year shall be issued upon payment of one-half (1/2) of
the annual fee; provided, that the applicant has not previously held a license
of the same type and class for which application is made. (1987 Code §
3-1-6)
4-1-6: TERM OF LICENSE:
The licenses shall be for a period of not exceeding one year, to terminate on
the first day of the fiscal year succeeding its issuance, where no provision to
the contrary is made. (1987 Code §
3-1-4)
4-1-7: POSTING LICENSE:
It shall be the duty of any person conducting a licensed business in the
Village to keep his license posted in a prominent place on the premises used
for such business at all times. (1987 Code § 3-1-9)
4-1-8: NONTRANSFERABILITY OF LICENSE; CHANGE OF LOCATION:
No license shall be assignable or transferable, nor shall any person be
authorized to do business or act under such license but the person to whom it
is granted or his administrator or executor, or at any other place than that
specified herein, nor shall any license authorize any person to act under it at
more than one place; provided, that any licensee conducting any business or
occupation required to be licensed who shall change the location of such place
of business before the expiration of such license, upon written notice to the
Village Clerk of the change in location, may continue said business at the new
location under said license previously issued unless otherwise restricted by
ordinance or law. (1987 Code § 3-1-7)
4-1-9: BUILDING AND PREMISES:
No license shall be issued for the conduct of any business, and no permit for
any thing or act, if the premises and building to be used for the purpose do
not fully comply with the requirements of the Village. No such license or
permit shall be issued for the conduct of any business or the performance of
any act which would involve a violation of the zoning title. (1987 Code § 3-1-
8)
4-1-10: NUISANCE BUSINESSES PROHIBITED:
No business, licensed or not, shall be so conducted or operated as to amount to
a nuisance in fact. (1987 Code § 3-1-10)
4-1-11: AUTHORITY TO GRANT LICENSES; SUSPENSION OR REVOCATION OF LICENSES:
The Village President may grant any license, and the Village President and
Board of Trustees may revoke any license issued under this chapter during the
term of such license for failure by any applicant or licensee to comply with
any provision of this Code or any Statutes of the State of Illinois relating to
the business, occupation or activity for which a license application has been
made or for which a license has been granted; provided, however, no license
shall be denied or revoked hereunder until notice has been given to the
applicant or licensee as provided in section
4-1-11-2 of this chapter, a reasonable time has elapsed to enable the applicant
or licensee to comply with the provisions of this Code and applicable State
Statutes, and the applicant or licensee has been given the opportunity to
present his case at a hearing as provided in section
4-1-11-3 of this chapter. Such denial or revocation of a license may be in
addition to any fine imposed. No person whose license has been revoked as
herein provided shall be eligible for a new license during the period for which
the revoked license was originally issued. (1987 Code § 3-1-11)
4-1-11-1: SUSPENSION OF LICENSE:
   A.   Authority Of Village President: The Village President may suspend, for
a period not to exceed thirty (30) days, any license issued under this chapter
during the term of such license upon conviction of the licensee of violation of
any provision of this Code or any Statutes of the State of Illinois relating to
the business, occupation or activity for which such license was issued.
   B.   Suspension Without Notice: The Village President may suspend for a
period not to exceed thirty (30) days, without prior warning, notice or
hearing, any license issued under this Code during the term of such license for
the failure of any licensee to comply with any provision of this Code or any
Statutes of the State of Illinois relating to the business, occupation or
activity for which such license was issued if, in the judgment of the Village
President, such failure constitutes an imminent danger to the public health,
safety or welfare.
   C.   Licensee To Cease Business Operations: Any person whose license is
suspended shall immediately discontinue the business, occupation or activity
for which the license was issued.
   D.   Hearing; Reinspection; Reinstatement:
      1.   Any person whose license is suspended may, at any time, either
petition in writing the Village President for a hearing or make written
application to the Village President for reinspection for the purpose of
reinstatement of the license. Any such hearing shall be held as soon as
possible and shall be conducted by and before the Village President at a time
and place designated by him. Based upon the record of such hearing, the Village
President shall make a finding and shall sustain, modify or rescind any
official notice or order considered in the hearing. A written report of the
hearing decision shall be furnished by the Village President to the person
whose license was suspended.
      2.   If a written application is made to the Village President for
reinspection for the purpose of reinstatement of the license, then, within ten
(10) days following receipt by the Village President of such application,
together with a written statement signed by the applicant that in the
applicant's opinion the conditions causing suspension of the license have been
corrected, the Village President shall cause a reinspection to be made.
      3.   If, after such reinspection, the applicant is found to comply with
all applicable provisions of this Code and Statutes of the State of Illinois,
his license shall be reinstated. (1987 Code § 3-1-11-1)
4-1-11-2: NOTICE OF LICENSE DENIAL OR REVOCATION:
   A.   When the Village President and Board of Trustees discover that there
has not been compliance with any of the applicable provisions of this Code or
any Statutes of the State of Illinois or they have been violated, the Village
President shall notify the applicant or licensee in writing of such
noncompliance or violation. Such notification shall: 1) set forth the specific
nature of the noncompliance or violation discovered; 2) establish a specific
and reasonable period of time for the correction of such noncompliance or
violation; 3) state that failure to comply with any notice issued in accordance
with the provisions of this Code may result in a denial or an immediate
revocation, as the case may be, of the license; and 4) state that an
opportunity for appeal from any notice or inspection findings will be provided
if a written request for a hearing is filed with the Village President and
Board of Trustees within the period of time established in the notice for
correction.
   B.   Any such notice shall be deemed to have been properly served when it
has been delivered personally to the applicant or licensee or when it has been
sent by registered or certified mail, return receipt requested, to the last
known residence or business address of the applicant or licensee. (1987 Code §
3-1-11-2)
4-1-11-3: HEARINGS ON LICENSE DENIAL OR REVOCATION:
The hearings on license denial or revocation matters shall be conducted by the
Village Board at a time and place designated thereby. Based upon the record of
such hearings, the Village President and Board of Trustees shall make a finding
and shall sustain, modify or rescind any official notice or order considered at
the hearing. A written report of the hearing decision shall be furnished to the
applicant or licensee by the Village President and Board of Trustees. (1987
Code § 3-1-11-3)
4-1-12: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter, where no other penalty is
specifically provided, shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code for each offense. A separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1987
Code § 3-1-12; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 2
ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES
SECTION:
4-2-1: State Regulations Adopted
4-2-2: Definitions
4-2-3: Administrative Officials

4-2-8: Classification Of Licenses
4-2-9: Number Of Licenses
4-2-10: License Fees
4-2-11: Term Of License
4-2-12: Transferability Of License; Change Of Location
4-2-13: Posting License; Duplicates
4-2-14: Open View From Street
4-2-15: Sanitary Conditions
4-2-16: Days And Hours Of Operation; Presence After Hours
4-2-17: Loitering Near Premises By Certain Persons Prohibited
4-2-18: Sales To Certain Persons Prohibited
4-2-19: Minors
4-2-20: Payment For Purchases Required
4-2-21: Additional Prohibited Acts Or Conditions
4-2-22: Inspections
4-2-23: Suspension Or Revocation Of License
4-2-24: Violations
4-2-25: Penalties
4-2-1: STATE REGULATIONS ADOPTED:
Each and every part of "an Act Relating to Alcoholic Liquors", enacted by the
General Assembly of the State, approved January 31, 1934, as the same is or may
be hereafter amended, which relates in any manner to the sale at retail of
alcoholic liquors, not heretofore used or adopted by reference or otherwise in
this chapter, is hereby adopted in this section and made a part of this
chapter, to the same extent and with the same legal effect as if fully set
forth herein, and any violation of such applicable and adopted provisions of
said Act shall be deemed a violation of this chapter and be subject to
penalties herein fixed. Three (3) copies of said Act shall be maintained on
file at the Office of the Village Clerk and shall be kept available for public
use, inspection and examination. (1987 Code § 3-6-17)
4-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
In addition to the definitions adopted by reference in section
4-2-1 of this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
set out in this section:
LICENSEE: Any person, firm, partnership, club, organization or corporation
receiving a license under this chapter.
LIQUOR: Any intoxicating malt, vinous, mixed or fermented liquor.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, club, organization or corporation.
RETAIL LIQUOR DEALER: Any "person", as defined herein, selling or offering for
sale or keeping with the intention of selling liquor at retail. (Ord. 18-2, 3-
13-2018; amd. 2018 Code)
4-2-3: ADMINISTRATIVE OFFICIALS:
   A.   Liquor Control Commissioner:
      1.   President Serve As: The Village President shall constitute and be
the Liquor Control Commissioner of the Village.
