      2.   Powers: Subject to the regulations and restrictions herein provided,
the President shall, as Liquor Control Commissioner, have the power to grant,
revoke and suspend licenses for sale at retail of any alcoholic beverages, and
to enter upon any licensed premises for inspection of the same in person or by
a police officer designated by him, and shall have such other powers relating
to liquor control as may be given him by ordinance or by law. (1987 Code § 3-6-
1-1)
   B.   Liquor Control Committee: The President shall appoint three (3)
Trustees who, together with the President, shall constitute the Liquor Control
Committee of the Village Board. Said Liquor Control Committee shall advise and
assist the Liquor Control Commissioner in the administration of the provisions
of this chapter. (1987 Code § 3-6-1-2)
4-2-4: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall sell, expose for sale or offer for sale at retail or display
within corporate limits of the Village any alcoholic liquor without first
obtaining a license from the Local Liquor Control Commissioner. (Ord. 18-2, 3-
13-2018)
4-2-5: INELIGIBILITY FOR LICENSE:
No such license shall be issued to any person:
   A.   Who is not a resident of the Village.
   B.   Who does not own the premises for which a license is sought or does not
have a valid lease thereon for the full period for which the license is to be
issued.
   C.   Who is not of good character and reputation in this community.
   D.   Who is in any manner disqualified from obtaining a State retail liquor
dealer's license under the laws of this State now in force relating to
alcoholic liquors or the nature of whose business or proposed business is such,
in the opinion of the Liquor Control Committee, that sale of liquor in
connection therewith will not be for the public good and convenience.
   E.   Who has failed to file with the application therefor, a policy of
insurance or satisfactory evidence that such policy of insurance has been
purchased and that the premium has been prepaid, insuring the applicant for
liability for: (1987 Code § 3-6-3-3)
      1.   Injury to one person: Five hundred thousand dollars ($500,000.00).
      2.   Injury to property: Fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00).
      3.   Recovery for means of support arising from death or injury to any
one person: Five hundred thousand dollars ($500,000.00).
      4.   Injury to person, property or loss of support in any one occurrence:
One million dollars ($1,000,000.00). (1987 Code § 3-6-3-3; amd. 2018 Code)
Said insurance policy shall list the Village as an additional party to receive
notice of cancellation of said policy. (1987 Code § 3-6-3-3)
4-2-6: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Applications for such licenses shall be made to the Village President in
writing, accompanied by the proper fee, and shall provide the following:
   A.   Name, age and address of an individual applicant.
   B.   The name of the person entitled to participate in the profits, if it is
a partnership application.
   C.   The objects, names and addresses of the officers and directors, if a
corporate application, and whether or not one person owns a controlling
interest in such corporation, and if so, his name and address.
   D.   The citizenship, place of birth and place of naturalization, if foreign
born, of an individual applicant.
   E.   The location and a description of the type or nature of the premises
where such liquor will be sold, served or consumed.
   F.   Whether or not any previous similar license has been applied for, the
place of application and the disposition of such application and if revoked,
the reason therefor.
   G.   Whether or not the applicant has ever been convicted of a felony, been
an inmate or keeper of a house of ill fame, or any offense opposed to decency
and morality.
   H.   No license shall be issued to any person ineligible under State law. A
manager or agent is required to have the same qualifications as the person or
firm to whom the license is issued. The names of all managers shall be listed
on said application.
   I.   All applications shall be verified by the applicant or if a
corporation, by an authorized officer thereof.
   J.   The application shall be accompanied by a license fee herein provided.
   K.   Where the applicant is not the owner of the premises, said application
shall be accompanied by a valid lease between the owner and the applicant for a
minimum period of one year to coincide with the period for which the
application is made.
   L.   The licensee will not violate any of the laws of the Municipality,
State or United States of America in the conduct of his business.
   M.   No licensee shall lease from or directly or indirectly receive or
accept from any manufacturer, distiller, brewer, bottler, wholesaler, jobber or
distributor, or from any agent or representative thereof, gratuitously any
money or thing of value nor shall said licensee borrow money from or permit
said person(s) to obtain directly or indirectly any interest in the ownership,
conduct or operation of the applicant's retail liquor business.
   N.   No license shall be issued to any applicant indebted to the Village,
County or any department thereof.
   O.   That the applicant agrees that, in case a license is issued, he will
not violate the terms and provisions of this chapter in any respect, and that
he will permit, at any time, the Village President or any members of the Liquor
Control Committee, or any police officer of the Village, without a warrant, to
enter the licensed premises and search the same for the purpose of determining
whether this chapter is being violated. (1987 Code § 3-6-3-2; amd. 2018 Code)
4-2-7: BOND REQUIREMENTS:
The applicant shall also enter into a bond payable to the Village in the penal
sum of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), said bond to be executed by the
applicant or applicants and by some incorporated surety company duly authorized
to execute bonds of that character in the State of Illinois, or by personal
sureties approved by the President and the Liquor Control Committee,
conditioned upon the faithful observance of the laws of the State of Illinois
and the provisions of this chapter. (1987 Code § 3-6-4)
4-2-8: CLASSIFICATION OF LICENSES:
Licenses shall be, and are hereby divided into classes, as follows:
   A.   Class A Licenses: Class A licenses shall entitle the licensee to sell
all kinds of alcoholic liquors for consumption on the premises where sold or in
package quantities.
   B.   Class C Licenses: Class C licenses may be issued only to clubs or
fraternal orders, either having a charter from a State or national organization
or operating under and by the authority of an order or society which is
Statewide or national in scope. (1987 Code § 3-6-5)
4-2-9: NUMBER OF LICENSES:
   A.   Class A Licenses: Class A licenses are limited to three (3) in number.
   B.   Class C Licenses: Class C licenses are limited to two (2) in number.
(1987 Code § 3-6-6)
4-2-10: LICENSE FEES:
   A.   The annual fees for licenses under this chapter shall be as follows:
      1.   Class A license: Five hundred dollars ($500.00).
      2.   Class C license: Twenty five dollars ($25.00). (Ord., 7-5-1988; amd.
2018 Code)
   B.   All such fees shall be paid to the President or the Village Clerk at
the time application is made, and shall be forthwith turned over to the Village
Treasurer. In the event the license applied for is denied, the fee shall be
returned to the applicant; but if the license is granted, then the fee shall be
deposited in the General Corporate Fund or in such other fund as shall have
been designated by the Board. (1987 Code § 3-6-7)
4-2-11: TERM OF LICENSE:
Each license issued under this chapter shall terminate at twelve o'clock (12:
00) midnight on April 30 next following its issuance, unless sooner revoked.
(1987 Code § 3-6-3-4)
4-2-12: TRANSFERABILITY OF LICENSE; CHANGE OF LOCATION:
   A.   Transferability Of License:
      1.   No license issued pursuant hereto shall be transferable except in
case of death of the licensee, whereupon said license shall be canceled unless
it is reissued upon proper application and in compliance with 235 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 5/16-1 to the spouse, heir at law or next of kin of the
licensee. (Ord. 18-2, 3-13-2018; amd. 2018 Code)
2. No license shall be transferred without the consent of the Local Liquor
Control Commissioner.
3. When a licensee sells or transfers his business to another, such successor
shall pay to the Village a fee equal to the sum of fifty dollars ($50.00) per
month or partial month remaining on said license before its expiration, up to a
maximum of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) in cases where an existing valid
license is reissued to such successor after he qualifies, for use at the same
location, in which event, the seller/licensee shall surrender his license for
cancellation which shall conclude his interest therein. The successor shall
first qualify and comply with all requirements of this chapter and pay in
advance for the reissuance of said license. (Ord. 18-2, 3-13-2018)
B. Change Of Location: A liquor dealer's license shall permit the sale of
alcoholic beverages only on the premises which is required to be described in
the application and license. Such location may be changed only upon the written
permission of the President and approval of the Liquor Control Committee and
which shall be issued by the Liquor Control Commissioner. No change of location
shall be permitted unless the proposed new location is a proper one for the
sale of alcoholic liquor under the laws of this State and the ordinances of the
Village. The fee to transfer use of a license from one location to another,
after permission is granted, shall be fifty dollars ($50.00). (1987 Code § 3-6-
3-6; amd. Ord. 18-2, 3-13-2018)
4-2-13: POSTING LICENSE; DUPLICATES:
Every person licensed in accordance with the provisions of this chapter shall
immediately post and keep posted while in effect, in a conspicuous place on the
premises, the license so issued. In the event such license shall be lost or
destroyed, a duplicate in lieu thereof shall be issued by the Village Clerk
upon direction of the Local Liquor Control Commissioner. The fee for the
duplicate license is fifty dollars ($50.00). (1987 Code § 3-6-12; amd. 2018
Code)
4-2-14: OPEN VIEW FROM STREET:
A. No curtains, drapes, screens, doors, partitions or view obstructing devices
shall be used or built within any establishment or premises used by any
licensee for sale of liquor, erected for the purpose of concealment or hiding
any person or patron in such establishment.
B. The interior doors of said licensed premises shall, at all times during
business hours, remain unlocked, and the exterior windows shall, at all times,
be maintained in a condition so as to afford an unobstructed view of the entire
interior of the premises from the exterior thereof during the hours that liquor
is sold therein. (1987 Code § 3-6-10)
4-2-15: SANITARY CONDITIONS:
A. Premises:
1. Sanitary measures for cleaning and caring for all glasses, dishes, utensils
and equipment shall be provided for by all licensees hereunder.
2. No license shall be granted to any applicant for the sale of intoxicating
liquors for consumption on the premises unless separate sanitary toilets for
men and women have been installed and provided on said premises, and such
toilets shall, at all times, be maintained in a clean and sanitary condition,
shall have hot and cold running water and shall be in compliance with all
Village ordinances.
B. Licensees And Employees: The licensees and the employees on premises used
for the retail sale of alcoholic liquor shall comply with the provisions of
State law relative to the health and cleanliness of employees selling food and
drink. (1987 Code § 3-6-11)
4-2-16: DAYS AND HOURS OF OPERATION; PRESENCE AFTER HOURS:
A. No holder of any license issued under the provisions of this chapter shall
sell any alcoholic liquor between the hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and nine
o'clock (9:00) A.M. on any day, other than Sunday, which shall be between the
hours of two o'clock (2:00) A.M. and ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. During such
closed hours, it shall be unlawful to consume, or to permit the consumption of,
or to sell, alcoholic liquor on any licensed premises.
B. No licensee shall permit any person or persons other than licensees or
employees to remain in the premises where liquor is offered for sale longer
than thirty (30) minutes after said closing hour. The hours herein stated shall
be the time prevailing in the Village (i.e., DST or CST). (1987 Code § 3-6-9)
4-2-17: LOITERING NEAR PREMISES BY CERTAIN PERSONS PROHIBITED:
No person under the age of twenty one (21) years unaccompanied by his or her
parents or legal guardian and no person who is intoxicated shall be permitted
to loiter about any licensed premises; provided, however, that this section
shall not apply to hotels, restaurants where regular meals are being served,
stores, clubs, bowling alleys, etc. (1987 Code § 3-6-14; amd. 2018 Code)
4-2-18: SALES TO CERTAIN PERSONS PROHIBITED:
No licensee shall sell, give or deliver alcoholic liquor to any minor or to any
intoxicated person, except as provided in 235 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/6-
16.1. (1987 Code § 3-6-14; amd. 2018 Code)
4-2-19: MINORS:
A. Purchasing: It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of twenty one
(21) years to purchase or obtain any alcoholic liquor in any tavern or other
place in the Village where alcoholic liquor is sold.
B. Misrepresentation Of Age: It shall be unlawful for any person under the age
of twenty one (21) years to misrepresent his or her age for the purpose of
purchasing or obtaining alcoholic liquor in any tavern or other place in the
Village where alcoholic liquor is sold.
C. Providing To: It shall be unlawful for any adult to give, sell or deliver to
any minor, directly or indirectly, any alcoholic liquor. (1987 Code § 3-6-14)
4-2-20: PAYMENT FOR PURCHASES REQUIRED:
Treating or giving away, directly or indirectly, of any intoxicating liquor
hereunder by the holder of any license at his place of business herein, by
either himself or by and through any servant, agent, employee or person on his
behalf, is hereby prohibited. (1987 Code § 3-6-15; amd. 2018 Code)
4-2-21: ADDITIONAL PROHIBITED ACTS OR CONDITIONS:
A. Consumption On Unlicensed Premises Or In Public:
1. No person shall bring any alcoholic liquor into any dining room of any
hotel, restaurant, club room or place where lunches are served, or where soft
drinks are sold or a soda fountain is operated, or into any public place for
consumption, or for use for mixing with or "spiking" any alcoholic liquor or
any other beverage whatsoever.
2. No owner or proprietor or agent or employee thereof of any restaurant, store
or other commercial establishment inviting or permitting public patronage,
shall permit the consumption of alcoholic liquors on the premises except those
specifically licensed for consumption on the premises.
3. No person shall consume any alcoholic liquor on any street, alley, sidewalk
or other public property or in any automobile or vehicle traveling upon or
parked on any street, alley or public property. (1987 Code § 3-6-16)
B. Gambling; Immorality:
1. No lottery except as authorized by 20 Illinois Compiled Statutes 1605/1 et
seq., of the Illinois Lottery Law, game of chance, gambling or gaming device,
except video gaming as permitted by 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 40/1 et
seq., shall be kept or used in any premises licensed hereunder nor shall any
licensee permit any illegal, disorderly or immoral practices upon the licensed
premises. (1987 Code § 3-6-16; amd. 2018 Code)
2. No person reputed to be a gambler or having been convicted of gambling or
having any connection with any alleged gambling house shall be granted a
license to sell alcoholic liquor. (1987 Code § 3-6-16)
4-2-22: INSPECTIONS:
All licensees are hereby required to make available for inspection by the Local
Liquor Control Commissioner and Police Committee Chairperson, or designee, the
premises where liquor is sold, served or consumed. (1987 Code § 3-6-13; amd.
2018 Code)
4-2-23: SUSPENSION OR REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The Local Liquor Control Commissioner may suspend or revoke any license issued
under this chapter for any one or more of the following reasons:
A. Violations of the laws of the United States government, the laws of the
State or any of the ordinances of the Village.
B. Knowingly permitting any violation of this chapter or any disorderly or
immoral practices upon the premises for which the license is issued.
C. Wilfully making any false statements as to a material fact in the
application for a license.
D. Failure of the licensee for any cause whatsoever to operate and maintain a
place of business at the location and on the premises pursuant to the purpose
for which the license was issued under this chapter.
E. Any license issued hereunder shall be kept continuously in effect and use in
any operative business during the period for which it is issued and when said
business is abandoned, closed or for any reason becomes inoperative for a
period of thirty (30) days or more, the Local Liquor Control Commissioner, in
his discretion, may revoke said license. (1987 Code § 3-6-18)
4-2-24: VIOLATIONS:
A. If the owner of the licensed premises or any person from whom the licensee
derives the right to possession of such premises, or the agent of such owner or
person, shall knowingly permit the licensee to use said licensed premises in
violation of the terms of this chapter, said owner, agent or other person shall
be deemed guilty of a violation of this chapter to the same extent as shall
said licensee and shall be subject to the same punishment as said licensee.
B. Every act or omission of whatsoever nature constituting a violation of any
of the provisions of this chapter by any officer, director, manager or agent or
employee of any licensee shall be deemed and held to be the act of such
employer or licensee and said employer or licensee shall be subject to
punishment in the same manner as if said act or omission had been done or
omitted by him personally. (1987 Code § 3-6-19)
4-2-25: PENALTIES:
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall, upon
conviction, be fined according to section
1-4-1 of this Code. Revocation or suspension of a license may be in addition to
the imposition of a fine or other penalty for violation of any of the
provisions of this chapter, and such revocation or suspension shall be no
defense to a prosecution for such violations. (1987 Code § 3-6-20)
CHAPTER 3
GAME MACHINES; VIDEO GAMING TERMINALS
SECTION:
4-3-1: Definitions
4-3-2: County And State Regulations Adopted
4-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and terms shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this
section:
CASINO GAME MACHINE: A game machine in which the game played is a mechanical or
video version of a traditional casino game including, but not limited to,
poker, craps, blackjack, slots, and roulette.
GAMBLING DEVICE: Any clock, tape machine, slot machine or other machines or
devices for the reception of money or other thing of value on chance or skill
or upon the action of which money or other thing of value is staked, hazarded,
bet, won or lost; or any mechanism, furniture, fixture, equipment or other
device designed primarily for use in a gambling place.
GAME MACHINE: A money-in-the-slot or coin-in-the-slot operated mechanical
device played for amusement which rewards the player with the right to replay
such mechanical device, or which allows the player to proceed to progressive
levels, which device is so constructed or devised as to make such result of the
operation depend in part upon the skill of the player and which returns to the
player thereof no money, property or right to receive money or property. The
term "game machine" shall include, but not be limited to, all devices commonly
known as video games, arcade games, or pinball machines. The term "game
machine" shall not include common parlor games such as pool, table tennis, and
darts. This definition is intended to be broadly construed, and all machines
that have mechanical parts that in any way resemble "game machines", as defined
herein, shall be licensed.
LICENSEE: Anyone licensed under this chapter.
PUBLIC GAME MACHINE PLACE: Any real estate, vehicle, boat, and/or property,
whatsoever, open to the public which contains one or more game machines. (Ord.
18-1, 3-13-2018; amd. 2018 Code)
4-3-2: COUNTY AND STATE REGULATIONS ADOPTED:
   A.   County Gambling Regulations: All sections of the Kankakee County
Municipal Code of 1981 concerning gambling, licensing, and penalties regarding
gambling machines in the County, sections 38-84, 38-85, and 38-86 of said Code,
are hereby adopted by reference.
   B.   State Video Gaming Act: The Illinois Video Gaming Act, 230 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 40/1 et seq., published as of May 2012, is hereby adopted by
reference. The gambling activity shall be conducted in complete compliance with
any and all requirements of said Act and in compliance with any and all rules,
regulations, opinions, and administrative decisions of the Illinois Department
of Revenue and/or the Illinois Gaming Board.
   C.   Copies On File: Copies of the regulations adopted in subsections A and
B of this section are on file in the Office of the Village Clerk for public use
and inspection. (Ord. 18-1, 3-13-2018; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 4
SOLICITORS AND PEDDLERS
SECTION:
4-4-1: Definitions
4-4-2: Exemptions From Provisions
4-4-3: Permit And License Required; Fee And Term
4-4-4: Verification Statement And Bond Requirements
4-4-5: Uninvited Soliciting Or Peddling
4-4-6: False Representation Prohibited
4-4-7: Street Intersection Soliciting
4-4-8: Penalty
4-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the following words and phrases shall have
the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this section:
PEDDLER: Every person who shall sell or offer for sale, barter or exchange any
goods, wares, merchandise, fruits, vegetables or produce by traveling from
place to place on, along or upon the streets, alleys or sidewalks of the
Village, or who shall sell and deliver any such items from any wagon, pushcart,
automobile or other vehicle going from place to place, or who shall go about
from place to place selling and delivering any such items.
SOLICITOR: Any person engaged in any one or more of the following activities:
   A.   Seeking to obtain either for immediate or future delivery, for the
purchase of goods, wares, merchandise, foodstuffs, services of any kind,
character or description whatever, for any kind of consideration whatever;
   B.   Seeking to obtain prospective customers for application or purchase of
insurance of any type, kind or character;
   C.   Seeking to obtain subscriptions to books, magazines, periodicals,
newspapers and every other type or kind of publication; or
   D.   Going upon any premises and ringing the doorbell upon or near any door,
or creating any sound in any manner calculated to attract the attention of the
occupant of such residence, for the purpose of engaging in any of the
activities described in subsections A, B and C of this definition. (1987 Code §
3-5-1)
4-4-2: EXEMPTIONS FROM PROVISIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the term "solicitor" or "peddler" shall not
include any person engaged in the following activities:
   A.   Seeking to obtain contributions on behalf of any charitable, religious,
civic, local fire or police auxiliary, school or scouting organization or any
other not for profit organization in good standing in the State;
   B.   Seeking to obtain signatures to petitions on political or public policy
questions or matters; or
   C.   Seeking to conduct any of the activities enumerated in section
4-4-1 of this chapter when undertaken by any person pursuant to a previous
appointment or invitation of the party being conducted. (1987 Code § 3-5-2)
4-4-3: PERMIT AND LICENSE REQUIRED; FEE AND TERM:
Before entering into any orders, sales or contracts, said peddler or solicitor
shall secure a permit from the Police Committee Chairperson and/or Village
Clerk certifying that there has been compliance with the provisions of this
chapter as set forth herein and fulfilled. Said permit shall then be deposited
with the Village Clerk and a license issued upon the payment of a fee of twenty
five dollars ($25.00), which license shall be valid for a period of one month.
(1987 Code § 3-5-8; amd. 2018 Code)
4-4-4: VERIFICATION STATEMENT AND BOND REQUIREMENTS:
Each such peddler or solicitor subject to the provisions of this chapter shall
file with the Police Committee Chairperson a verification statement of his
residence, the principal or employer's name and address and the assets and
liabilities of said peddler or solicitor. In addition thereto, the peddler or
solicitor shall give and enter into a proper and suitable bond to the Village
in the penal sum of two thousand dollars ($2,000.00), signed by responsible
sureties or a surety company and conditioned that said peddler or solicitor
fully and faithfully will secure performance of his part of all sales and
contracts made by him and will account for all monies so received by him and
will reimburse each of his said purchasers or contractors, if the principal of
the peddler or solicitor repudiates the authority of the peddler or solicitor,
or refuses, without lawful reason, to complete and fulfill his part of the
order, sale or contract. (1987 Code § 3-5-7; amd. 2018 Code)
4-4-5: UNINVITED SOLICITING OR PEDDLING:
   A.   No person shall engage in soliciting or peddling upon any premises or
in any dwelling house, apartment or other residence located thereon within the
Village after having been asked by the owner or occupant thereof to leave such
premises or residence, nor shall any person engage in solicitation or peddling
upon any premises or in any dwelling house, apartment or other residence
located thereon if such premises or building is posted against solicitation or
peddling by means of a notice prominently displayed, upon which is printed one
of the following:
   NO SOLICITORS OR PEDDLERS
   or
   NO TRESPASSING
   B.   The above notice shall be posted or exhibited at or near the main
entrance to the premises or on or near the main door to any dwelling or
residence thereon or at any point of approach or entry thereto. (1987 Code § 3-
5-3)
4-4-6: FALSE REPRESENTATION PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any peddler or solicitor to solicit orders, or
to make sales of goods, merchandise, magazines, services or wares, or to enter
into contracts, where any money or other valuable consideration is sought,
asked for or received in advance from any person within the Village and before
the entire completion and fulfillment of the order, sale or contract on the
part of the peddler or solicitor, or his principal, unless said peddler or
solicitor in fact represents the principal for whom he purports to act, and
unless the said peddler or solicitor further supplies satisfactory proof that
he will and is financially able to account for all monies and considerations
received by him in advance on said order, sale or contract. (1987 Code § 3-5-6)
   B.   The Police Committee Chairperson, in his discretion and at the expense
of the peddler or solicitor, may telephone, telegraph or otherwise communicate
with the alleged principal to verify the alleged agency. (1987 Code § 3-5-6;
amd. 2018 Code)
4-4-7: STREET INTERSECTION SOLICITING:
   A.   Eligibility To Solicit: No charitable or not for profit organization or
other person shall conduct solicitation activities on or within any of the
street intersections within the Village, unless such organization shall be:
      1.   Registered with the Attorney General as a charitable organization in
the manner provided by law.
      2.   Engaged in Statewide fundraising activities.
      3.   Liable for any injuries to any person or property during such
solicitation activity which is casually related to an act of ordinary
negligence of the soliciting agent.
      4.   Liable for any increase in the cost of liability insurance taken by
the Village with respect to said street intersection solicitation activity.
      5.   Restricted in its solicitation activities to representatives or
agents who shall be eighteen (18) years of age or more and who shall be wearing
a high visibility vest, with no more than four (4) such persons being allowed
to actually solicit on or within an intersection at any one time.
      6.   Able to first furnish a valid certificate of liability insurance
with an insurer approved by the Village naming the Village as an additional
insured with respect to such solicitation activities.
      7.   Able to first execute a hold harmless and indemnification agreement
with the Village with respect to such solicitation activities. (1987 Code § 3-
5-4)
   B.   Permission Required: Any organization eligible to conduct solicitation
activities shall obtain permission for such solicitation from the Police
Committee Chairperson. It shall be the duty of the Police Committee Chairperson
to see that the applicant complies with eligibility requirements contained in
subsection A of this section, and in addition, the Police Committee Chairperson
must also find that the locations, times and durations of the proposed
solicitation activity and the number of proposed solicitors shall not result in
an interference with the flow of vehicular traffic or otherwise create a
hazardous and unsafe condition at any such street intersection. (1987 Code § 3-
5-5; amd. 2018 Code)
4-4-8: PENALTY:
All violations of this chapter shall be enforced in accordance with section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1987 Code § 3-5-9)
TITLE 5
HEALTH, SANITATION AND ENVIRONMENT
CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
SECTION:
5-1-1: Nuisances Enumerated
5-1-2: Nonsummary Abatement
5-1-3: Summary Abatement
5-1-1: NUISANCES ENUMERATED:
The following acts, conduct and conditions are hereby declared and defined to
be nuisances, and when committed, performed or permitted to exist by any
individual, firm, association or corporation within the territorial limits of
the Village are hereby declared to be unlawful and prohibited:
   A.   Any act or offense which is a nuisance according to the common law of
the State of Illinois or declared or defined to be a nuisance by the ordinances
of the Village. In addition, the officials of the Village shall be authorized
to abate any nuisance which, while not specifically defined within this
chapter, shall constitute the unreasonable, unwarrantable or unlawful use by a
person of property, real or personal, or from his own improper, indecent or
unlawful personal conduct which works an obstruction or injury to a right of
another, or of the public, and produces such material annoyance, inconvenience,
discomfort or hurt that the law will presume an actionable nuisance. Nuisances
may be abated which are public or which are both public and private in nature.
   B.   To cause or suffer the carcass of any animal or any offal, filth or
noisome substance to be collected, deposited or to remain in any place under
his ownership or control to the prejudice of others.
   C.   To throw or deposit any offal or other offensive matter, or the carcass
of any dead animal in any watercourse, lake, pond, spring, well or common
sewer, street, alley, public highway, churches, school premises, or park.
   D.   To corrupt or render unwholesome or impure the water of any spring,
river, stream, pond or lake, to the injury or prejudice of others.
   E.   To obstruct or encroach upon public highways, private ways, streets,
alleys, commons, landing places, and ways to burying places.
   F.   To erect, continue or use any building or other place for the exercise
of any trade, employment or manufacture, which, by occasioning noxious
exhalations, offensive smells or otherwise, is offensive or dangerous to the
health of individuals, or of the public.
   G.   To advertise wares or occupations by painting notices of the same on,
or affixing them to fences, walls, windows, building exteriors, utility poles,
or on hydrants, other public or private property, or rocks or other natural
objects, without the consent of the owner, or if in the highway or other public
place, without permission of the proper authorities.
   H.   To harass, intimidate or threaten any person who is about to sell or
lease or has sold or leased a residence or other real property or is about to
buy or lease or has bought or leased a residence or other real property, when
the harassment, intimidation or threat relates to a person's attempt to sell,
buy or lease a residence, or other real property, or refers to a person's sale,
purchase or lease of a residence or other real property.
   I.   To dump, abandon, deposit, dismantle or burn upon any public property
or right-of-way, highway, park, street, or parkway anywhere in the Village, any
trash, garbage, ashes, junk, junked or wrecked motor vehicles or parts thereof,
or miscellaneous waste. (1987 Code §
8-1-1)
   J.   To store, keep or maintain outside of a closed building, any junk,
parts, machinery or equipment not in an operable condition, or motor vehicle
not in an operable condition, where such inoperable motor vehicle is an actual
danger or detriment to life, safety, health or peaceful enjoyment of the
property of surrounding landowners. (1987 Code §
8-1-1; amd. 2018 Code)
   K.   To own, maintain or keep a dwelling unit unfit for human habitation, or
dangerous or detrimental to life, safety or health because of lack of repair,
defects in the plumbing system, lighting or ventilation, the existence of
contagious diseases or unsanitary conditions likely to cause sickness among
persons residing in said premises or residing in proximity thereof.
   L.   To store or place any materials in a manner which may harbor rats.
   M.   To produce or permit to be produced, whether on public or private
property, any offensive noise to the disturbance of the peace or quiet of any
person residing in the vicinity.
   N.   To stockpile firewood unless same is stacked in an orderly fashion, off
the ground, and on a hard surface.
   O.   To grade, fill, excavate or otherwise alter real property in a manner
which causes an unreasonable amount of water to be discharged on adjoining
property.
   P.   To locate or maintain a stable, pigsty, or privy within the corporate
limits of the Village.
   Q.   To locate or maintain at any place within the Village or within a
radius of one mile from the corporate limits and without the Village, any
slaughterhouse, packing house, rendering establishment or bone factory; or to
suffer or permit any premises at any place within the corporate limits to
become foul or offensive.
   R.   To permit foul or stagnant water to stand upon any premises to the
prejudice of others.
   S.   To suffer any cellar, vault, drain, privy, yard or premises to become,
for any cause, foul or offensive or injurious to public health.
   T.   To suffer any premises where any animal is kept to become nauseous,
foul or offensive to any neighborhood, family or person.
   U.   To deposit or permit to remain on any premises or public street or
alley, slops or animal or vegetable matter of any kind, which is likely to
become putrid and offensive. (1987 Code §
8-1-1)
5-1-2: NONSUMMARY ABATEMENT:
   A.   Notice Requirements: Except where otherwise provided by the ordinances
of the Village, any officer of the Village possessing police powers may serve
or cause to be served a notice, in writing, upon the owner, agent, occupant or
person in possession, charge or control of any lot, building or premises or
item of personalty in or upon which any nuisance exists, requiring them or
either or both of them, to abate the same within a specified reasonable time,
in such manner as the notice shall direct. (1987 Code § 
8-1-2)
   B.   Procedure: If the person so served and notified does not abate the
nuisance within the specified reasonable time, the Corporate Authorities may
proceed to abate the nuisance in any or all manner allowable by law, including,
without limiting the generality thereof, the following:
      1.   Seeking to impose a monetary penalty under section
1-4-1 of this Code by instituting an ordinance enforcement action.
      2.   Seeking to enjoin the continuation of the nuisance by the filing of
a lawsuit in a court of competent jurisdiction. (1987 Code §
8-1-3)
5-1-3: SUMMARY ABATEMENT:
Whenever, in the opinion of an officer of the Village possessing police powers,
the maintenance or continuation of a nuisance creates an imminent threat of
serious injury to persons or serious damage to personal or real property, or if
the nuisance can be abated summarily without or with only minor damage to the
items or premises which are creating the nuisance, then the continuation of the
nuisance poses a substantial threat of injury to person or property or
substantial interference with the quiet enjoyment of life normally present in
the community, such officer shall proceed to abate such nuisance; provided,
further, that whenever the owner, occupant, agent or person in possession,
charge or control of the real or personal property which has become a nuisance
is unknown or cannot readily be found, the Village officer with police power
may proceed to abate such nuisance without notice. Where the abatement of the
nuisance requires continuing acts by the Corporate Authorities beyond the
initial summary abatement and any other additional emergency abatements, it
shall seek abatement of such nuisance on a permanent basis through judicial
process as soon as reasonably possible. (1987 Code §
8-1-4)
CHAPTER 2
VEGETATION CONTROL
SECTION:
5-2-1: Weeds Declared A Nuisance And Prohibited
5-2-2: Height Restriction
5-2-3: Removal Notice
5-2-4: Abatement By Village; Costs
5-2-1: WEEDS DECLARED A NUISANCE AND PROHIBITED:
Any weeds such as jimson, burdock, ragweed, thistle, cocklebur or other weeds
of a like kind, found growing in any lot or tract of land in the Village are
hereby declared to be a nuisance, and it shall be unlawful to permit any such
weeds to grow or remain in any such place. (1987 Code § 8-5-1)
5-2-2: HEIGHT RESTRICTION:
It shall be unlawful for anyone to permit any weeds, grass or plants, other
than trees, bushes, flowers or other ornamental plants to grow to a height
exceeding eight inches (8") anywhere in the Village. Any such plants, grass or
weeds exceeding such height are hereby declared to be a nuisance. (Ord., 8-3-
1996)
5-2-3: REMOVAL NOTICE:
It shall be the duty of the Police Committee Chairperson to serve or cause to
be served a notice upon the owner or occupant of any premises on which plants,
grass or weeds are permitted to grow in violation of the provisions of this
chapter and to demand the abatement of the nuisance within ten (10) days. (1987
Code § 8-5-3; amd. 2018 Code)
5-2-4: ABATEMENT BY VILLAGE; COSTS:
   A.   Abatement By Village: If the person so served does not abate the
nuisance within ten (10) days, any Village Board member may proceed to abate
such nuisance, keeping an account of the expense of the abatement, and such
expense shall be charged and paid by the owner or occupant. If the Village is
responsible for the abatement, there will be a two hundred dollar ($200.00)
charge each time abatement is required. (1987 Code § 8-5-4; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Costs A Lien: Charges for such plant, grass or weed removal shall be a
lien upon the premises. Whenever a bill for such charges remains unpaid for
thirty (30) days after it has been rendered, the Village Clerk may file with
the County Recorder of Deeds a statement of lien claim. This statement shall
contain a legal description of the premises, the expenses and costs incurred
and the date the plants, grass or weeds were cut, and a notice that the Village
claims a lien for this amount. Notice of such lien claim shall be mailed to the
owner of the premises if his address is known; provided, however, that failure
of the Village Clerk to record such lien claim or to mail such notice, or the
failure of the owner to receive such notice, shall not affect the right to
foreclose the lien for such charges as provided herein. (1987 Code § 8-5-5)
   C.   Foreclosure Of Lien:
      1.   Property subject to a lien for unpaid plant, grass or weed cutting
charges shall be sold for nonpayment of the same, and the proceeds of such sale
shall be applied to pay the charges after deducting costs, as is the case in
the foreclosure of statutory liens. Such foreclosure shall be in equity in the
name of the Village.
      2.   The Village Attorney is hereby authorized and directed to institute
such proceedings, in the name of the Village in any court having jurisdiction
over such matter, against any property for which such bill has remained unpaid
sixty (60) days after it has been rendered. (1987 Code § 8-5-6)
CHAPTER 3
LITTER CONTROL
SECTION:
5-3-1: Definitions
5-3-2: Use Of Receptacles Required
5-3-3: Sidewalks To Be Kept Clear; Prohibitions
5-3-4: Private Property
5-3-5: Parks
5-3-6: Additional Prohibitions
5-3-7: Penalty
5-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words and their
derivations shall have the meanings given herein. When not inconsistent with
the context, words used in the present tense include the future, words used in
the plural number include the singular number, and words used in the singular
number include the plural number. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not
merely directory.
GARBAGE: Putrescible animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling,
preparation, cooking and consumption of food.
LITTER: "Garbage", "refuse" and "rubbish" as defined herein and all other waste
material which, if thrown or deposited as herein prohibited, tends to create a
danger to public health, safety and welfare.
PARK: A park, playground, recreation center or any other public area in the
Village, owned or used by the Village and devoted to active or passive
recreation.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind.
PRIVATE PREMISES: Any dwelling, house, building or other structure designed or
used either wholly or in part for private residential purposes, whether
inhabited or temporarily or continuously uninhabited or vacant, and shall
include any yard, grounds, walk, driveway, porch, steps, vestibule or mailbox
belonging or appurtenant to such dwelling, house, building or other structure.
PUBLIC PLACE: Any and all streets, sidewalks, boulevards, alleys or other
public ways and any and all public parks, squares, spaces, grounds and
buildings.
REFUSE: All putrescible and nonputrescible solid wastes, except body wastes,
including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street cleanings, dead animals, abandoned
automobiles, and solid market and industrial wastes.
RUBBISH: Nonputrescible solid wastes consisting of both combustible and
noncombustible wastes, such as paper, wrappings, cigarettes, cardboard, tin
cans, yard clippings, leaves, wood, glass, bedding, crockery and similar
materials.
VEHICLE: Every device in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be
transported or drawn upon a highway, including devices used exclusively upon
stationary rails or tracks.
VILLAGE: The Village of Buckingham, Illinois. (1987 Code § 8-4-1)
5-3-2: USE OF RECEPTACLES REQUIRED:
   A.   No person shall throw or deposit litter in or upon any street, sidewalk
or other public place within the Village, except in public receptacles, in
private receptacles for collection or in official Village dumps.
   B.   Persons placing litter in receptacles or in private receptacles shall
do so in such manner as to prevent it from being carried or deposited by the
elements upon any street, sidewalk or other public place or upon private
property. (1987 Code § 8-4-2)
5-3-3: SIDEWALKS TO BE KEPT CLEAR; PROHIBITIONS:
   A.   1. No person shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other
public place within the Village the accumulation of litter from any building or
lot or from any public or private sidewalk or driveway.
      2.   Persons owning or occupying property shall keep the sidewalk in
front of their premises free of litter.
   B.   1. No person owning or occupying a place of business shall sweep into
or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the Village, the
accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private
sidewalk or driveway.
      2.   Persons owning or occupying places of business within the Village
shall keep the sidewalk in front of their business premises free of litter.
(1987 Code § 8-4-3)
5-3-4: PRIVATE PROPERTY:
   A.   Occupied Private Property:
      1.   No person shall throw or deposit litter on any occupied private
property within the Village, whether owned by such person or not; except, that
the owner or person in control of private property may maintain private
receptacles for collection in such a manner that litter will be prevented from
being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk or other
public place or upon any private property.
      2.   The owner or person in control of any private premises shall, at all
times, maintain the premises free of litter; provided, however, that this
subsection shall not prohibit the storage of litter in private receptacles for
collection.
   B.   Vacant Private Property: No person shall throw or deposit litter on any
open or vacant private property within the Village, whether owned by such
person or not. (1987 Code § 8-4-7)
   C.   Clearing From Open Private Property By Village:
      1.   Notice To Remove: The Police Committee Chairperson is hereby
authorized and empowered to notify the owner of any open or vacant private
property within the Village or the agent of such owner to properly dispose of
litter located on such owner's property which is dangerous to public health,
safety or welfare. Such notice shall be by registered mail, addressed to said
owner at the address listed on the Village records or by affixing the same in a
conspicuous position on said premises.
      2.   Action Upon Noncompliance: Upon the failure, neglect or refusal of
any owner or agent so notified to properly dispose of litter dangerous to the
public health, safety or welfare within ten (10) days after receipt of written
notice provided for in subsection C1 of this section, or within ten (10) days
after the posting of the premises as herein provided, the Police Committee
Chairperson is hereby authorized and empowered to pay for the disposing of such
litter or to order its disposal by the Village. (1987 Code § 8-4-7; amd. 2018
Code)
      3.   Costs:
         a.   Bill For Service; Failure To Pay: When the Village has effected
the removal of such dangerous litter or has paid for its removal, the actual
cost thereof, plus accrued interest at the rate of ten percent (10%) per annum
from the date of the completion of the work, if not paid by said owner prior
thereto, shall be charged to the owner of such property on the next regular
bill forwarded to such owner by the Village, and said charge shall be due and
payable by said owner at the time of payment of such bill.
         b.   Costs A Lien: Where the full amount due the Village is not paid
by such owner within sixty (60) days after the disposal of such litter as
provided in subsections C1 and C2 of this section, then and in that case, the
Village Clerk shall cause to be recorded in the Office of the County Recorder
of Deeds a sworn statement showing the cost and expense incurred for the work,
the date the work was done and the location of the property on which said work
was done. The recording of such sworn statement shall constitute a lien and
privilege on the property, and shall remain in full force and effect for the
amount due in principal and interest, plus costs of court, if any, for
collection until final payment has been made. Said costs and expenses shall be
collected in the manner fixed by law for the collection of taxes and further
shall be subject to a delinquency penalty of ten percent (10%) in the event the
same is not paid in full on or before the date the tax bill upon which said
charge appears becomes delinquent. Sworn statements recorded in accordance with
the provisions hereof shall be prima facie evidence that all legal formalities
have been complied with and that the work has been done properly and
satisfactorily, and shall be full notice to every person concerned that the
amount of the statement, plus interest, constitutes a charge against the
property designated or described in the statement and that the same is due and
collectible as provided by law.
   D.   Garbage Containers And Pick Up:
      1.   Placement For Pick Up: For those property owners/renters who have no
alley access from which garbage and rubbish may be collected, their garbage and
rubbish container must be kept at the rear of their property until no sooner
than the night before the scheduled pick up, at which time, containers may be
placed at the right-of-way line for pick up.
      2.   Removal After Pick Up: All property owners/renters who have placed
their garbage or rubbish containers at the right-of-way line for pick up must
remove said container no later than the night of the scheduled pick up and
place said container at the rear of their property. (1987 Code § 8-4-7)
      3.   Collection Fee: For garbage collection, the Village shall charge the
rates set out in subsection 8-3-4B of this Code. (Ord., 9-7-1996; amd. 2018
Code)
5-3-5: PARKS:
   A.   Litter In Parks Generally: No person shall throw or deposit litter in
any park within the Village, except in public receptacles and in such a manner
that the litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the
elements upon any part of the park or upon any street or other public place.
Where public receptacles are not provided, all such litter shall be carried
away from the park by the person responsible for its presence and properly
disposed of elsewhere as provided herein.
   B.   Bodies Of Water: No person shall throw or deposit litter in any
fountain, pond, stream or any other body of water in a park or elsewhere within
the Village. (1987 Code § 8-4-6)
5-3-6: ADDITIONAL PROHIBITIONS:
   A.   Throwing From Vehicle: No person, while a driver or passenger in a
vehicle, shall throw or deposit litter upon any street or other public place
within the Village or upon private property. (1987 Code § 8-4-4)
   B.   Spilling Loads; Mud And Dirt Deposits: No person shall drive or move
any truck or other vehicle within the Village unless such vehicle is so
constructed or loaded as to prevent any load, contents or litter from being
blown or deposited upon any street, alley or other public place. Nor shall any
person drive or move any vehicle or truck within the Village, the wheels or
tires of which carry onto or deposit in any street, alley or other public
place, mud, dirt, sticky substances, litter or foreign matter of any kind.
(1987 Code § 8-4-5)
   C.   Depositing Tires: The dumping or depositing of tires is hereby declared
a nuisance and prohibited within the Village.
   D.   Improper Depositing: It shall be a violation of this chapter for any
person or entity to place, deposit or leave for pick up any solid waste or any
recyclable materials on any property not owned or occupied by that person
without the consent of the property owner.
   E.   Exterior Storage: No person in charge of or in control of premises,
whether as owner, lessee, tenant, occupant or otherwise, shall allow any
lumber, junk, trash, debris, abandoned, discarded or unused objects or
equipment such as furniture, stoves, refrigerators, freezers, cans or
containers to remain on such property longer than five (5) days. (Ord. 12-2, 2-
6-2012)
5-3-7: PENALTY:
Any person violating any portion of this chapter shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code, and each day such violation is committed or permitted to
continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable hereunder
as such. (1987 Code § 8-4-8; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 4
OPEN BURNING
SECTION:
5-4-1: Authority To Prohibit Burning
5-4-2: Permitted Hours
5-4-3: Hazardous Burns
5-4-4: Burning Leaves
5-4-5: Exemptions
5-4-1: AUTHORITY TO PROHIBIT BURNING:
The Village Board shall prohibit any or all bonfires and outdoor rubbish fires
when atmospheric conditions or local circumstances make such fires hazardous.
(1987 Code § 8-6-6)
5-4-2: PERMITTED HOURS:
All outdoor burning in the Village not otherwise excepted herein shall be done
between seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. and eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. (1987 Code §
8-6-1; amd. 2018 Code)
5-4-3: HAZARDOUS BURNS:
It shall be unlawful to light or maintain any fire in the Village so close to
any building, structure, utility pole, wires of utility companies, fences,
automobiles or trucks so as to create a fire hazard. (1987 Code § 8-6-2)
5-4-4: BURNING LEAVES:
The conditions of the burning of leaves shall be:
   A.   All leaf fires are to be supervised at all times by the occupant, owner
or tenant or by such person designated thereby.
   B.   All leaf fires shall be kept at a minimum distance so as not to
endanger property or lives.
   C.   It shall be unlawful for any person to burn leaves upon any bituminous
or asphalt pavement, public sidewalk or on any street or alley on which it is
prohibited by Village ordinance. (1987 Code § 8-6-4)
5-4-5: EXEMPTIONS:
It is not the intent of this chapter to prohibit the use of outdoor fireplaces,
barbecue pits or burners for the preparation of food or bonfires, provided such
use creates no fire hazard or public nuisance. (1987 Code § 8-6-5)
CHAPTER 5
ABANDONED, INOPERABLE VEHICLES
SECTION:
5-5-1: Definitions
5-5-2: Nuisances Declared And Prohibited
5-5-3: Notice To Abate
5-5-4: Abatement By Village
5-5-5: Impoundment And Disposition Of Vehicles
5-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions shall apply in the interpretation and enforcement of
the chapter:
INOPERABLE MOTOR VEHICLE: A. A motor vehicle which has to be licensed and
registered, i.e., automobile, truck, motorcycle, motorized camper, which for at
least one month, the engine, wheels, or other parts have been removed, altered,
damaged, or otherwise so treated that the vehicle is incapable of being used as
designed.
   B.   A motor vehicle is deemed to be inoperable if either of the following
occurs:
1. No valid registration is issued for said vehicle for a period of one month.
2. No movement of the vehicle under its own power for a period of at least one
month if such registration is necessary for the operation on a street or
highway.
   C.   "Inoperable motor vehicle" shall not include a motor vehicle which, in
order to perform ordinary service or repair operations, has been rendered
temporarily incapable of being used as designed for a period not to exceed one
month, and any vehicle that has been completely covered over by a proper
covering, i.e., tarp, etc.
PROPERTY: Any real property within the Village which is not a street or
highway.
STREET OR HIGHWAY: The entire width between the boundary lines of every way
publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for
the purposes of vehicular travel.
VEHICLE: A machine propelled by power other than human power designed to travel
along the ground by use of wheel, and transport persons or property or pull
machinery and shall include, without limitation, automobiles, trucks,
motorcycles, and motorized campers. (Ord. 02-2, 5-14-2002; amd. 2018 Code)
5-5-2: NUISANCES DECLARED AND PROHIBITED:
The following acts, conduct and conditions are hereby declared and defined to
be a nuisance and when committed, performed or permitted to exist by any person
within the limits of the Village, are hereby declared to be unlawful and
prohibited:
   A.   To store, keep or maintain outside of a closed building any inoperable
vehicle unless the vehicle is completely covered with a proper covering.
   B.   To abandon any vehicle within the Village limits.
   C.   To leave any vehicle at any place within the Village for such time and
under such circumstances as to cause the vehicle to reasonably appear to have
been abandoned.
   D.   To leave any partially dismantled, inoperable, wrecked or junked
vehicle on any street or highway within the Village. (Ord. 02-2, 5-14-2002)
5-5-3: NOTICE TO ABATE:
The Village Clerk, pursuant to authorization by the Village Board, police, and/
or Police Committee Chairperson, may serve or cause to be served a notice in
writing upon the owner, agent, occupant or person in possession, charge or
control of any vehicle, which appears to be in violation of this chapter or
upon the owner, agent, occupant or person in possession, charge or control of
any lot, building or premises in or upon which any inoperable vehicle in
violation of this chapter is situated, requiring him to remove the same within
a specified reasonable time, not to exceed thirty (30) days. If not removed,
will be removed pursuant to subsection 5-5-5B of this chapter. (Ord. 02-2, 5-
14-2002; amd. 2018 Code)
5-5-4: ABATEMENT BY VILLAGE:
If the person so served and notified does not remove or cover properly the
motor vehicle within the specified reasonable time, the Village may proceed to
abate the nuisance in any manner allowable including:
   A.   Seeking to impose a monetary penalty as defined by subsection 5-5-5A of
this chapter for enforcement action.
   B.   Seeking to enjoin the continuation of the nuisance created by the
presence of the motor vehicle by the filing of a lawsuit in a court of
jurisdiction. (Ord. 02-2, 5-14-2002)
5-5-5: IMPOUNDMENT AND DISPOSITION OF VEHICLES:
   A.   Impoundment: The Village Board, Police Committee Chairperson, or any of
the Police Department designated by the Village Board, is hereby authorized to
remove or have removed any vehicle left at any place within the Village which
reasonably appears in violation, or which reasonably appears to be lost, stolen
or unclaimed, or which is an inoperable vehicle as defined in this chapter. The
vehicles which are removed will be at the owner's burden of cost. (Ord. 02-2,
5-14-2002)
   B.   Disposition: The procedure to be followed by the Village Board, Police
Committee Chairperson, and/or the Police Department for disposition in regard
to abandoned, lost, stolen, or unclaimed vehicles will be in accordance with
625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/4-202; provided, that no vehicle shall be
returned until all fees and costs incurred by the Village have been paid in
full. (Ord. 02-2, 5-14-2002; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 6
STORAGE TANKS
SECTION:
5-6-1: Underground Storage Tanks Prohibited
5-6-2: Aboveground Storage Tanks
5-6-1: UNDERGROUND STORAGE TANKS PROHIBITED:
Underground storage tanks used for the dispensing or storage of gasoline,
diesel fuel, and volatile oils are strictly forbidden in the Village corporate
limits. (Ord. 17-11, 12-5-2017)
5-6-2: ABOVEGROUND STORAGE TANKS:
   A.   Restrictions: As of January 1, 2018, an aboveground storage tank or
tanks (AST) used for the dispensing or storage of gasoline, diesel fuel, and
volatile oils and which does not have a current State of Illinois - Illinois
State Fire Marshal permit, will not be allowed in the Village corporate limits.
After January 1, 2018, no aboveground storage tanks used for dispensing or
storage of gasoline, diesel fuel, and volatile oils will be allowed in the
Village corporate limits.
   B.   Compliance With State Regulations: If there are any aboveground storage
tanks in the Village corporate limits, they must have a current State of
Illinois Fire Marshal permit and follow all State of Illinois - State of
Illinois Fire Marshal rules and regulations concerning aboveground storage
tanks. (Ord. 17-11, 12-5-2017)
TITLE 6
POLICE AND PUBLIC SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
6-1-1: Department Established; Residency
6-1-2: Chain Of Command
6-1-3: Employees Of Department
6-1-4: Supervision Of Department
6-1-5: Duties Of Department Employees
6-1-6: Compensation
6-1-1: DEPARTMENT ESTABLISHED; RESIDENCY:
There is hereby established a Police Department for the Village which shall
consist of such employees as may be provided by the Board of Trustees.
Employees of the department shall not be required to be residents of the
Village. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-1-2: CHAIN OF COMMAND:
The chain of command is as follows: Chief of Police, Chairman of the Police
Committee, Village President and Board of Trustees. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-1-3: EMPLOYEES OF DEPARTMENT:
The employees of the department shall be employed by the Village President, by
and with the consent of the Board of Trustees. The Village President, by and
with the consent of the Board of Trustees, may designate one such employee of
the department as the Chief of Police. Employees of the department shall work
such hours each week as designated by the Chief of Police, but not to exceed
the maximum number of hours established by the Board of Trustees or Village
President, unless previously specifically authorized in writing by the Village
President. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-1-4: SUPERVISION OF DEPARTMENT:
Employees of the department shall be under the supervision and control of the
Village President, pursuant to authority granted herein; provided, that if a
Chief of Police is designated, the Chief shall be responsible for the
supervision of the other employees of the department. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-1-5: DUTIES OF DEPARTMENT EMPLOYEES:
   A.   It shall be the duty of the employees of the department to see to the
enforcement of all of the ordinances of the Village and all statutes applicable
therein, and to preserve order and prevent infractions of the law and arrest
violators thereof and to perform such other duties as the President and Board
of Trustees shall prescribe for the preservation of the peace and the
observance of the ordinances and laws.
   B.   It shall be the duty and obligation of employees of the department to
follow all rules and regulations set forth by the Chief, President and Board of
Trustees as shall be deemed advisable for the operation of the department.
   C.   It shall be the duty and obligation of every employee of the department
to conduct himself or herself in a proper and law abiding manner, at all times,
to obey the directions of his or her supervisor and to avoid the use of any
unnecessary force. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-1-6: COMPENSATION:
Employees of the department shall be paid such compensation as determined by
the President and Board of Trustees. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
CHAPTER 2
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
6-2-1: Livestock Prohibited
6-2-2: Cruelty To Animals
6-2-3: Noisy Animals
6-2-4: Diseased Domestic Animals
6-2-5: Dangerous, Vicious Animals
6-2-6: Impoundment And Redemption Provisions
6-2-1: LIVESTOCK PROHIBITED:
Livestock, defined as any hoofed animal, are not allowed in the Village
corporate limits. (2018 Code)
6-2-2: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully or maliciously torture, destroy
or kill or cruelly beat or injure, maim or mutilate any animal in subjugation
or captivity, whether wild or tame, and whether belonging to himself or to
another, or to deprive any such animal of necessary food, drink or shelter or
veterinary care to prevent suffering; to cause, procure or permit any such
animal to be so tortured, destroyed or killed, or cruelly beaten or injured,
maimed or mutilated, or deprived of necessary food, drink or shelter or
veterinary care to prevent suffering; or wilfully instigate, engage in or in
any way further any act of cruelty to any animal, or any act tending to produce
such cruelty. (2018 Code)
6-2-3: NOISY ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful to harbor or keep any animal which disturbs the peace by
loud noises at any time of the day or night. (1987 Code §
9-4-3)
6-2-4: DISEASED DOMESTIC ANIMALS:
A. No domestic animal afflicted with a contagious or infectious disease shall
be allowed to run at large, or to be exposed in any public place whereby the
health of man or beast may be affected; nor shall such diseased animal be
shipped or removed from the premises of the owner thereof, except under the
supervision of the County Health Officer or the State Veterinarian. No such
diseased animals shall be brought into the Village. (1987 Code §
9-4-4)
B. It is hereby made the duty of the Police Committee Chairperson to secure
such disposition of any diseased animal and such treatment of affected premises
as to prevent the communication and spread of the contagion or infection,
except in the cases where the State Veterinarian is empowered to act. (1987
Code §
9-4-4; amd. 2018 Code)
6-2-5: DANGEROUS, VICIOUS ANIMALS:
A. Running At Large: It shall be unlawful to permit any dangerous animal or
vicious animal of any kind to run at large within the Village. (1987 Code § 9-
4-7)
B. Permit For Exhibitions And Parades: Exhibitions or parades of animals which
are ferae naturae in the eyes of the law may be conducted only upon securing a
permit from the Police Committee Chairperson.
C. Authority To Kill: The members of the Village Board or the Police Committee
Chairperson is authorized to kill any dangerous animal of any kind when it is
necessary for the protection of any persons or property. (1987 Code § 9-4-7;
amd. 2018 Code)
D. Animals That Bite: Any animal which has bitten any person or so injured any
person as to have caused an abrasion of the skin, or is suffering from rabies,
shall be subject to the procedures applicable to dogs under article A of this
chapter. (1987 Code § 9-4-7)
6-2-6: IMPOUNDMENT AND REDEMPTION PROVISIONS:
The Kankakee County animal control ordinance regulates the impoundment and
redemption of animals in the Village. (2018 Code)
ARTICLE A. DOGS
SECTION:
6-2A-1: Definition
6-2A-2: License Required; Tag
6-2A-3: Number Of Dogs; Kennels And Breeders Prohibited
6-2A-4: Dogs At Large; Impoundment
6-2A-5: Dogs That Bite; Rabies Control
6-2A-6: Removal Of Excrement Required
6-2A-7: Dogs In Heat
6-2A-8: Dangerous, Vicious Dogs
6-2A-9: Penalty; Court Order To Destroy Dog
6-2A-1: DEFINITION:
The word "dog", whenever used in this article, shall include a female as well
as a male dog. (1987 Code §
9-3-1)
6-2A-2: LICENSE REQUIRED; TAG:
   A.   License Required; County To Provide: No person shall own or keep a dog
unless he shall procure a license from the County therefor. All provisions of
the County animal control ordinance with respect to licenses are made a part
hereof and incorporated herein by this reference. (1987 Code §
9-3-2)
   B.   Collar And Tag: Every dog kept within the Village shall be provided by
its owner or kept with a collar made of leather, metal or substantial material
to which a license tag shall be fastened. (1987 Code §
9-3-3)
6-2A-3: NUMBER OF DOGS; KENNELS AND BREEDERS PROHIBITED:
No more than four (4) dogs can be kept in a residential residence. Over four
(4) animals is considered a breeder, which is not permitted within the Village
corporate limits. Running a kennel is not permitted within the Village
corporate limits. (Ord. 17-3, 1-3-2017)
6-2A-4: DOGS AT LARGE; IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   If the County Animal Control is called for a dog at large, and the
County Animal Control does not pick up the dog or animal, and if the animal's
owner is known, then the owner will be charged the fee that the County Animal
Control charges the Village, plus a Village administrative fee of one hundred
dollars ($100.00). If the fee/penalty/fine has not been paid within fourteen
(14) days from the date of letter to the owner from the Village, then the fee/
penalty/fine will be doubled. For each consecutive fourteen (14) day period
following that the fee/penalty/fine is not paid, the fee/penalty/fine is
doubled.
   B.   In agreement with the County Animal Control, if a dog or animal has
been picked up by County Animal Control, the dog/animal will not be released to
the owner before all Village fees/penalties/fines have been paid in full to the
Village. The owner of the dog/animal must bring a receipt from the Village to
the County Animal Control which has the Village Clerk's signature thereon.
(Ord. 15-2, 11-3-2015)
   C.   It shall be the duty primarily of the Police Committee Chairperson or
in his absence any member of the Village Board to take up and impound any dog
found running at large in the Village contrary to this article. All dogs so
found running at large shall be delivered to the County Dog Pound, and all
provisions contained in the County animal control ordinance with respect to the
impounding of dogs, the redemption thereof, and the disposal of unclaimed
impounded dogs are made a part hereof and incorporated herein by this
reference. (1987 Code §
9-3-4; amd. 2018 Code)
6-2A-5: DOGS THAT BITE; RABIES CONTROL:
The Kankakee County animal control ordinance regulates biting dogs and rabies
in the Village. (2018 Code)
6-2A-6: REMOVAL OF EXCREMENT REQUIRED:
   A.   Owner's Premises: It shall be unlawful for any person to create a
nuisance whereby the animal excrement of any dog lies unattended and
uncollected by the owner or keeper of a dog housed in a pen or chained to a
stake within the Village, and any person who permits a violation of this
subsection shall be served by any Village Board member with an official notice
and shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code for each violation. (1987 Code § 9-3-11; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Public And Private Property:
      1.   No person shall appear with a dog upon the public ways or within
public places or upon the property of another, without that person's consent
and without some means for the removal of excrement; nor shall any person fail
to remove any excrement deposited by such dog.
      2.   It shall be the duty of each person who owns, possesses or controls
a dog to remove and dispose of any feces left by such person's dog on any
sidewalk, street, or other public area. It shall be the duty of each person who
owns, possesses or controls a dog to remove and dispose of any feces left by
such person's dog on any private property neither owned nor occupied by the
person.
      3.   For the purpose of this subsection B, the means of removal shall be
any tool, implement, bag, or other device for the purpose of picking up and
containing such feces. Disposal shall be accomplished by transporting the feces
to a place suitable for the disposal of dog feces.
      4.   Violation of this subsection B shall be punishable by a fine not
exceeding:
         a.   Ten dollars ($10.00) for the first offense.
         b.   Twenty five dollars ($25.00) for the second offense within a year
of the first offense.
         c.   Fifty dollars ($50.00) for the third and any subsequent offenses
within a year of the first offense.
      5.   This subsection B shall not apply to a licensed dog accompanying any
person with a disability who, because of such person's disability, is
physically unable to comply with the requirements of this subsection B. (2018
Code)
6-2A-7: DOGS IN HEAT:
Any person owning or controlling any female dog or any person at whose house or
premises, building, store or dwelling place any female dog is usually found or
permitted to remain, shall not permit or suffer it to run at large in any
public way or public place while it is in heat, whether it has a license or
muzzle on or not. Every female dog so found running at large is hereby deemed a
nuisance, and shall be taken up and impounded in the manner provided by this
article, but if such dog cannot be safely taken up and impounded, it may be
slain by any police officer. (1987 Code §
9-3-8; amd. 2018 Code)
6-2A-8: DANGEROUS, VICIOUS DOGS:
Any dangerous, fierce or vicious dogs running at large in the public ways or
public places in the Village or upon private premises of any person other than
the owner or keeper, and any dog which may in any manner disturb the quiet of
any person or neighborhood, or which shall bite a person or so injure a person
as to cause an abrasion of the skin, is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and
such dog shall be taken up and impounded in the manner provided by this
article. (1987 Code §
9-3-9)
6-2A-9: PENALTY; COURT ORDER TO DESTROY DOG:
   A.   If at the time and place set for trial in any court for any cause
referred to in this article, it shall appear that any dog has in any manner
disturbed the quiet of any person, or caused an abrasion of the skin, or
attempted to bite or snap at any person within the Village, the owner or keeper
shall be deemed to have violated this article and shall be subject to the
penalty provided for violation in section
6-2A-4 of this article. (1987 Code § 9-3-10)
   B.   The court may stay execution or issuance of a mittimus upon motion of
the Village Attorney and continue the cause for a further day, and order the
defendant to have the dog destroyed by the Kankakee Animal Control Officer
within the time for which the case is continued. Upon a satisfactory showing to
the court that the dog has been destroyed, the court may, in its discretion,
cause a nonsuit to be entered in said cause. (1987 Code § 9-3-10; amd. 2018
Code)
ARTICLE B. CHICKENS
SECTION:
6-2B-1: Purpose
6-2B-2: Permitted And Prohibited Chickens
6-2B-3: Noncommercial Use Only
6-2B-4: Maximum Number Of Hens
6-2B-5: Containment Of Feed
6-2B-6: Enclosures
6-2B-7: Chicken Runs
6-2B-8: Care Of Chickens
6-2B-9: Odor And Noise
6-2B-10: Predators, Rodents, Insects And Parasites
6-2B-11: Prohibited Acts
6-2B-12: Violations; Penalty
6-2B-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this article is to provide standards for the keeping of
domesticated chickens. It is intended to enable residents to keep a small
number of female chickens while creating standards and requirements that ensure
that domesticated chickens do not adversely impact the neighborhood surrounding
the property on which the chickens are kept. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-2: PERMITTED AND PROHIBITED CHICKENS:
   A.   Permitted Chickens: Within the Village limits, only female chickens
(hens) are allowed. There is no restriction on chicken species.
   B.   Roosters Prohibited: Roosters are not allowed within the Village
limits. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-3: NONCOMMERCIAL USE ONLY:
Chickens shall be kept for personal use only. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-4: MAXIMUM NUMBER OF HENS:
The maximum number of hens allowed within the Village limits is eight (8) total
per residence. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-5: CONTAINMENT OF FEED:
All food must be kept in airtight containers that are out of reach of wild
animals. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-6: ENCLOSURES:
Hens must be provided with an enclosure, such as a henhouse, chicken tractor,
or chicken coop, that houses them. Enclosures must be clean, dry, and odor
free. Enclosures shall be kept in a neat and sanitary condition at all times in
a manner that will not disturb the use or enjoyment of neighboring lots due to
noise, odor or other adverse impact. Coop size should be four (4) square feet
per bird with a maximum of thirty six (36) square feet. Enclosures are not
permitted in the front yard of any property. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-7: CHICKEN RUNS:
The hens must be provided with an outdoor fenced structure in which to run
around. The hens have to be in a fenced area at all times, unable to leave the
residents' property. The maximum size of the chicken run should be no more than
eighty (80) square feet. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-8: CARE OF CHICKENS:
Hens must be properly cared for. Chickens must be provided with the access to
feed and clean water at all times. The feed and water shall be unavailable to
rodents, wild birds, and predators. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-9: ODOR AND NOISE:
   A.   Odors from chickens, chicken manure, and other chicken related
substances shall not be perceptible at the property boundaries.
   B.   Perceptible noise from chickens shall not be loud enough at the
property boundaries to disturb persons of reasonable sensitivity. (Ord. 17-12,
12-5-2017)
6-2B-10: PREDATORS, RODENTS, INSECTS AND PARASITES:
The property/chicken owner shall take all necessary action to reduce the
attraction of predators and rodents. Infestation of insects and parasites that
may result in unhealthy conditions to human habitation will result in the
chicken facility being removed by the Village through the Kankakee County
Animal Control Officer, Village Animal Control Officer, or any other designee,
and the cost of the same shall be borne by the property/chicken owner. (Ord.
17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-11: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   Slaughtering: There will be no slaughtering of chickens within the
Village limits.
   B.   Bird Fights: Raising or keeping hens for fighting and the fighting of
hens and other fowl is not allowed within the Village. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
6-2B-12: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
Each violation of this article shall be subject to a daily twenty five dollar
($25.00) fine. Each day a violation continues shall constitute a separate
offense. The Village shall retain the right to inspect any property to
determine whether a violation has been corrected. (Ord. 17-12, 12-5-2017)
ARTICLE C. COUNTY ANIMAL CONTROL REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-2C-1: County Regulations Adopted
6-2C-2: Amendments To Regulations
6-2C-1: COUNTY REGULATIONS ADOPTED:
Chapter 10, animals, and the fees in chapter 18 applicable to animals of the
Kankakee County animal control regulations are hereby adopted by reference as
if fully set out at length herein. Three (3) copies of said regulations are on
file in the Office of the Village Clerk for public use and inspection. (Ord.
17-3, 1-3-2017; amd. 2018 Code)
6-2C-2: AMENDMENTS TO REGULATIONS:
If there should be any changes or amendments to chapter 10 and the fees in
chapter 18 of the Kankakee County animal control regulations applicable to
animals after the effective date hereof, the changes or amendments will be
automatically adopted under this section. (Ord. 17-3, 1-3-2017; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 3
GENERAL OFFENSES
ARTICLE A. OFFENSES RELATED TO PERSONS, HEALTH AND SAFETY
SECTION:
6-3A-1: Assault
6-3A-2: Battery
6-3A-3: Unlawful Conduct
6-3A-4: Disorderly Conduct
6-3A-5: Reckless Conduct
6-3A-6: Mob Action
6-3A-7: Throwing Missiles
6-3A-8: Weapons
6-3A-9: Resisting Or Interfering With Police
6-3A-10: Abusive Language; Obscene Gestures
6-3A-1: ASSAULT:
   A.   A person commits an assault when, without lawful authority, he
assaults, beats, wounds, strikes, imprisons or inflicts violence on another
where the circumstances show malice or assault with intent to commit any
misdemeanor or felony.
   B.   No person shall assault another with a lethal weapon, instrument or
thing with intent to commit upon the person of another any bodily injury where
no considerable provocation appears or where the circumstances of the assault
show malice.
   C.   If any person shall be guilty of an assault within the Village, such
person shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined not less than four hundred
dollars ($400.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each offense
and be responsible for the Village costs of prosecution. Each day that a
violation continues shall be considered a separate offense. Restitution by the
violator shall also be made to any property damaged or destroyed or person
injured. (Ord., 4-8-1997)
6-3A-2: BATTERY:
   A.   A person commits battery if he intentionally or knowingly without legal
justification and by any means:
      1.   Causes bodily harm to an individual; or
      2.   Makes physical contact of an insulting or provoking nature with an
individual.
   B.   If any person shall be guilty of any battery within the Village, such
