person shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined according to the provisions of
section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1987 Code §
9-1-2)
6-3A-3: UNLAWFUL CONDUCT:
   A.   A person commits unlawful conduct when that person disturbs, tends to
disturb or aids in disturbing the peace of others by violent, tumultuous,
offensive or obstreperous conduct, and no person shall knowingly permit such
conduct upon any premises owned or possessed by him or under his control.
(Ord., 4-8-1997)
   B.   Any person, firm or corporation violating this section shall be fined
as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code for each offense and shall be responsible for the Village
costs of prosecution. Each day that a violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. Restitution by the violator shall also be made to any
property damaged or destroyed or person injured. (Ord., 4-8-1997; amd. 2018
Code)
6-3A-4: DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
   A.   Definition: Any of the following acts shall, when committed within the
Village, be considered as disorderly conduct:
      1.   Commits an act in a violent manner toward another whereby that other
is placed in danger of his life or health.
      2.   Commits an act in a violent manner toward another whereby the
property of any person is placed in danger of being destroyed or damaged.
      3.   Causes, provokes or engages in any fight, brawl or riotous act so as
to endanger the life, health or property of another.
      4.   Interferes with another's pursuit of a lawful occupation by acts of
violence.
      5.   Obstructs, either singly or together with other persons, the flow of
vehicular or pedestrian traffic and refuses to clear such public way when
ordered to do so by the Police Department or other lawful authority.
      6.   Resists or obstructs the performance of duties by the Police
Department or any other authorized Village official.
      7.   Incites, attempts to incite or is involved in attempting to incite
imminent lawless action including rioting, fighting and other unlawful
disturbances.
      8.   Uses abusive language or makes threats to any member of the Police
Department, any other authorized Village official who is engaged in the lawful
performance of his duties, or any other person when such words have a direct
tendency to cause acts of violence. Words merely causing displeasure, annoyance
or resentment are not prohibited.
      9.   Damages, befouls or disturbs public property or the property of
another so as to create a hazardous, unhealthy, or physically offensive
condition.
      10.   Makes or causes to be made any loud, boisterous and unreasonable
noise or disturbance to the annoyance of any other persons nearby, or near to
any public highway, road, street, lane, alley, park, square or common, whereby
the public peace is broken or disturbed, or the travelling public annoyed.
      11.   Fails to obey a lawful order to disperse by a police officer where
one or more persons are committing acts of disorderly conduct in the immediate
vicinity, and the public health and safety is threatened.
      12.   Assembles with one or more persons for the purpose of using force
or violence to disturb the peace.
      13.   Appears in any public place and is manifestly under the influence
of alcohol, narcotics or other drugs, not therapeutically administered, to the
degree that he may endanger himself or other persons or property, or alarm or
disturb other persons in his vicinity.
      14.   Transmits in any manner to any police officer, public officer or
public employee a report to the effect that an offense has been committed,
knowing at the time of such transmission that there is no reasonable ground for
believing that such an offense has been committed.
      15.   Uses paint or other medium in any way to deface, damage or destroy
property, structures, buildings, bridges, fences, streets, sidewalks, hydrants,
streetlights, or signs.
      16.   To be openly lewd or do any act of public indecency tending to
debauch the public morals.
      17.   To interrupt or disturb any lawful assembly or procession of people
met for a lawful purpose.
      18.   To injure, beat, torture or kill any animal or knowingly allow same
to be done to any animal under one's personal control, unless such is necessary
to protect the health or safety of oneself or another.
      19.   To make or cause to be made any annoying, obscene or disturbing
phone calls.
      20.   To transmit in any manner to the Fire Department of any city, town,
village or fire protection district a false alarm of fire, knowing at the time
of such transmission that there is no reasonable ground for believing that such
fire exists.
      21.   To transmit in any manner to another a false alarm to the effect
that a bomb or other explosive of any nature is concealed in such place that
its explosion would endanger human life, knowing at the time of such
transmission that there is no reasonable ground for believing that such bomb or
explosive is concealed in such place. (Ord., 4-8-1997)
   B.   Prohibited; Penalties: It is hereby declared to be unlawful for any
person to engage in any type of disorderly conduct within the Village as
defined herein. Any person violating this section shall be fined as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this Code for each offense and shall be responsible for the Village
costs of prosecution. Each day that a violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. Restitution by the violator shall also be made regarding any
property damaged or destroyed or person injured. (Ord., 4-8-1997; amd. 2018
Code)
6-3A-5: RECKLESS CONDUCT:
A person who causes bodily harm to or endangers the bodily safety of an
individual by any means, commits reckless conduct if he performs recklessly the
acts which cause harm or endanger safety, whether they otherwise are lawful or
unlawful. If any person shall be guilty of reckless conduct within the Village,
such person shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined according to the
provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1987 Code §
9-1-4)
6-3A-6: MOB ACTION:
A person commits mob action when he or she engages in any of the following:
   A.   The knowing or reckless use of force or violence disturbing the public
peace by two (2) or more persons acting together and without authority of law;
   B.   The knowing assembly of two (2) or more persons with the intent to
commit or facilitate the commission of a misdemeanor; or
   C.   The knowing assembly of two (2) or more persons, without authority of
law, for the purpose of doing violence to the person or property of anyone
supposed to have been guilty of a violation of the law, or for the purpose of
exercising correctional powers or regulative powers over any person by
violence. (2018 Code)
6-3A-7: THROWING MISSILES:
No person shall throw, shoot or cast any stone or any other missile upon or at
any building or tree or other public or private property, or upon or at any
person in any street, avenue, alley, public place or enclosed or unenclosed
ground in the Village, or aid or abet in the same. (1987 Code §
9-1-7)
6-3A-8: WEAPONS:
   A.   Firearms:
      1.   Discharging Restricted: It shall be unlawful to discharge any
firearms or air gun in the Village. This subsection shall not be considered to
prohibit any officer of the law from discharging a firearm in the performance
of his duty or any citizen from discharging a firearm when lawfully defending
his person or property. A violator of this subsection shall be punishable by a
fine according to the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code.
      2.   Furnishing To Minors: It shall be unlawful for any person to loan or
furnish to any minor, not being the father, guardian or employer of such minor,
any gun, pistol or any other firearm. A violator of this subsection shall be
punishable by a fine according to the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
   B.   Bows And Arrows: No person shall purposefully or heedlessly shoot or
cause to be shot any arrow, projectile, or other missile from a bow from or
into any public place, or at any house, vehicle, property, person or animal. A
violator of this subsection shall be punishable by a fine according to the
provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-3A-9: RESISTING OR INTERFERING WITH POLICE:
No person shall resist any police officer in the discharge of his duty or fail
or refuse to obey any lawful command of any such officer or in any way
interfere with or hinder or prevent any officer from discharging his duty, or
in any manner assist or give aid to any person in the custody of a police
officer in attempting to escape from such custody, or rescue or attempt to
rescue any person when in such custody. If any person shall be guilty of
resisting or interfering within the Village, such person shall, upon conviction
thereof, be fined according to the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-3A-10: ABUSIVE LANGUAGE; OBSCENE GESTURES:
Use of abusive language or threats to any member of the Police Department, any
other authorized Village official who is engaged in the lawful performance of
his duties, or any other person when such words have a direct tendency to cause
acts of violence is prohibited. Words merely causing displeasure, annoyance or
resentment are not prohibited. Use of abusive or obscene language or making of
an obscene gesture in public likely to incite immediate physical retaliation by
the hearer will be considered disorderly conduct. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
ARTICLE B. OFFENSES RELATED TO MORALS AND DECENCY
SECTION:
6-3B-1: Sex Offenses; Statute Provisions Adopted
6-3B-2: Loitering; Wandering
6-3B-3: Public Intoxication
6-3B-4: Narcotic Drugs
6-3B-1: SEX OFFENSES; STATUTE PROVISIONS ADOPTED:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of regulating and controlling sex
offenses within the Village, 720 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11.01 et seq.
Said provisions of the Illinois Criminal Code, supplements, appendices and
amendments are adopted by reference. Pursuant to 65 Illinois Compiled Statutes
5/1-3-2, the Village Clerk is directed to certify three (3) copies of the
hereinabove adopted provisions of the Illinois Criminal Code and maintain said
copies on file in the Office of the Village Clerk. (1987 Code §
9-1-6; amd. 2018 Code)
6-3B-2: LOITERING; WANDERING:
   A.   A person loitering or strolling in, about or upon any street, alley or
other public way or public place, or in any public gathering or assembly, or in
or around any store, shop or business or commercial establishment, or in the
private property or place without lawful business, or conducts himself in a
lewd, wanton or lascivious manner in speech or behavior, shall be guilty of
loitering.
   B.   Wandering the streets, alleys or other public ways or other places at
late or unusual hours in the night without any visible or lawful business and
not giving a satisfactory account of himself shall be guilty of being abroad at
unusual hours. (Ord., 4-8-1997)
   C.   Any person, firm or corporation violating this section shall be fined
as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code for each offense and be responsible for the Village costs of
prosecution. Each day that a violation continues shall be considered a separate
offense. Restitution by the violator shall also be made regarding any property
damaged or destroyed or person injured. (Ord., 4-8-1997; amd. 2018 Code)
6-3B-3: PUBLIC INTOXICATION:
Any person found in a state of intoxication in any street, avenue, alley,
highway or thoroughfare or other public place to the degree that he may
endanger himself or other persons or property, or alarm or disturb other
persons in his vicinity shall be guilty of public intoxication. (1987 Code §
9-1-3; amd. 2018 Code)
6-3B-4: NARCOTIC DRUGS:
   A.   Prohibition: Except as allowed by law, no person in the Village shall
sell, give away, use or possess for any purpose, whatever, any narcotic drug.
(Ord., 5-4-1996)
   B.   Seizures:
      1.   Narcotic Drugs: All narcotic drugs in the possession of any person
convicted of a violation of this section shall be seized by, confiscated by and
forfeited to the Police Committee Chairperson who shall make proper
distribution thereof.
      2.   Vehicle: Any vehicle from which seized drugs are removed, the
vehicle being owned by the person convicted of a violation of this section,
shall be seized by, confiscated by and forfeited to the Police Committee
Chairperson and subsequently sold at public auction to the highest bidder in
the manner provided by law. (Ord., 5-4-1996; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 4
GANG ACTIVITY
SECTION:
6-4-1: Temporary Questioning Without Arrest
6-4-2: Search For Weapons
6-4-3: Defacing Property
6-4-4: Penalty
6-4-1: TEMPORARY QUESTIONING WITHOUT ARREST:
A police officer, after having identified himself as a police officer, may stop
any person in a public place for a reasonable period of time when the person is
wearing known gang colors, emblems or other gang insignia, or appears to be
engaged in communicating gang related messages through the use of hand signals
or other means of communication, or as otherwise provided by law, and the
officer reasonably infers from the circumstances that the person is committing,
is about to commit or has committed any offense set forth in this section. Once
stopped, the officer may demand the name and address of the person and an
explanation of his actions. Such detention and temporary questioning will be
conducted in the vicinity of where the person was stopped. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-4-2: SEARCH FOR WEAPONS:
When a police officer has stopped a person for temporary questioning pursuant
to section
6-4-1 of this chapter and the officer reasonably suspects that he or another
officer is in danger of attack, he may search the person(s) for weapons. If an
officer discovers a weapon, he may take it until the completion of the
questioning, at which time, he shall return the weapon, if lawfully possessed,
or arrest the person so questioned. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
6-4-3: DEFACING PROPERTY:
Uses of paint or other medium in any way to deface, damage or destroy property
will be determined disorderly conduct. (Ord., 5-4-1996; amd. 2018 Code)
6-4-4: PENALTY:
Any person found guilty of violating any provision of this chapter shall be
fined according to the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., 5-4-1996)
CHAPTER 5
FIREWORKS AND EXPLOSIVES
SECTION:
6-5-1: Fireworks
6-5-2: Nitroglycerine And TNT Storage
6-5-3: Explosives Storage And Sale
6-5-1: FIREWORKS:
   A.   Public Fireworks Displays:
      1.   Permit Required: No public exhibition of fireworks or pyrotechnics
shall be given unless a permit therefor is first secured from the Village
Board. (1987 Code § 8-2-1-1)
      2.   Supervision: All such public displays shall be under the supervision
of a competent person, and shall be superintended by a member of the Village
Board. (1987 Code § 8-2-1-1; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Prohibitions:
      1.   Discharge Of Fireworks: It shall be unlawful to discharge or set off
any fireworks, or make or give any pyrotechnic display in the Village unless a
permit has been obtained as provided herein. (1987 Code § 8-2-1-2)
      2.   Sale Of Fireworks: No person shall sell or offer for sale, or keep
for the purpose of so doing, any fireworks. (1987 Code § 8-2-1-3)
      3.   Certain Fireworks Prohibited: No person shall discharge or set off
in the Village, or keep in the Village with the intention of doing so, any
firecrackers, toy cannons, canes for exploding potash, sulphur or other
dangerous explosive; so called Chinese bombs; torpedoes; paper balloons; or sky
rockets rated at one pound or over; provided, that the fireworks mentioned in
this subsection may be used in any licensed public pyrotechnic display under
proper supervision. (1987 Code § 8-2-1-4)
6-5-2: NITROGLYCERINE AND TNT STORAGE:
It shall be unlawful to keep or store any nitroglycerine or the explosive
commonly known as TNT in the Village in any quantities, excepting for medicinal
or laboratory purposes, and for such purposes no more than one pound shall be
stored in any one building or premises. (1987 Code §
8-2-2)
6-5-3: EXPLOSIVES STORAGE AND SALE:
All explosives must be kept, stored and sold in accordance with State law and
in accordance with the rules enforced by the State Fire Marshal with regard to
the same. (1987 Code § 8-2-3; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 6
MINORS
SECTION:
6-6-1: Curfew Regulations
6-6-1: CURFEW REGULATIONS:
   A.   Definitions: When used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
    CURFEW HOURS: 1. Between one minute after twelve o'clock (12:01) A.M. and
six o'clock (6:00) A.M. on Saturday;
      2.   Between one minute after twelve o'clock (12:01) A.M. and six o'clock
(6:00) A.M. on Sunday; and
      3.   Between eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. on Sunday to Thursday,
inclusive, and six o'clock (6:00) A.M. on the following day.
   EMERGENCY: An unforeseen combination of circumstances or the resulting state
that calls for immediate action. The term includes, but is not limited to, a
fire, a natural disaster, an automobile accident, or any situation requiring
immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life.
   ESTABLISHMENT: Any privately owned place of business operated for a profit
to which the public is invited including, but not limited to, any place of
amusement or entertainment.
   GUARDIAN: 1. A person who, under court order, is the guardian of the person
of a minor; or
      2.   A public or private agency with whom a minor has been placed by a
court.
   MINOR: Any person under seventeen (17) years of age.
   PARENT: A person who is:
      1.   A natural parent, adoptive parent, or stepparent of another person;
or
      2.   At least eighteen (18) years of age and authorized by a parent or
guardian to have the care and custody of a minor.
   PUBLIC PLACE: Any place to which the public or a substantial group of the
public has access and includes, but is not limited to, streets, highways, and
the common areas of schools, hospitals, apartment houses, office buildings,
transport facilities, and shops.
   REMAIN: To:
      1.   Linger or stay; or
      2.   Fail to leave premises when requested to do so by a police officer
or the owner, operator, or other person in control of the premises.
   SERIOUS BODILY INJURY: Bodily injury that creates a substantial risk of
death or that causes death, serious permanent disfigurement, or protracted loss
or impairment of the function of any bodily member or organ.
   B.   Offenses:
      1.   A minor commits a curfew offense when he or she remains in any
public place or on the premises of any establishment during curfew hours.
      2.   A parent or guardian of a minor or other person in custody or
control of a minor commits a curfew offense when he or she knowingly permits
the minor to remain in any public place or on the premises of any establishment
during curfew hours.
   C.   Defenses: It is a defense to prosecution under subsection B of this
section that the minor was:
      1.   Accompanied by the minor's parent or guardian or other person in
custody or control of the minor;
      2.   On an errand at the direction of the minor's parent or guardian,
without any detour or stop;
      3.   In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
      4.   Engaged in an employment activity or going to or returning home from
an employment activity, without any detour or stop;
      5.   Involved in an emergency;
      6.   On the sidewalk abutting the minor's residence or abutting the
residence of a next door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the
Police Department or a Village Board member about the minor's presence;
      7.   Attending an official school, religious, or other recreational
activity supervised by adults and sponsored by a government or governmental
agency, a civic organization, or another similar entity that takes
responsibility for the minor, or going to or returning home from, without any
detour or stop, an official school, religious, or other recreational activity
supervised by adults and sponsored by a government or governmental agency, a
civic organization, or another similar entity that takes responsibility for the
minor;
      8.   Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the United States
Constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, and the
right of assembly; or
      9.   Married or had been married or is an emancipated minor under the
Emancipation of Minors Act.
   D.   Enforcement: Before taking any enforcement action under this section, a
law enforcement officer shall ask the apparent offender's age and reason for
being in the public place. The officer shall not issue a citation or make an
arrest under this section unless the officer reasonably believes that an
offense has occurred and that, based on any response and other circumstances,
no defense in subsection C of this section is present.
   E.   Violation; Penalties: A violation of this section is a petty offense
with a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code; except, that neither a person who has been made a ward of
the court under the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, nor that person's legal
guardian, shall be subject to any fine. In addition to or instead of the fine
imposed by this subsection, the court may order a parent, legal guardian, or
other person convicted of a violation of subsection B of this section to
perform community service as determined by the court; except, that the legal
guardian of a person who has been made a ward of the court under the Juvenile
Court Act of 1987 may not be ordered to perform community service. The dates
and times established for the performance of community service by the parent,
legal guardian, or other person convicted of a violation of subsection B of
this section shall not conflict with the dates and times that the person is
employed in his or her regular occupation. (2018 Code)
CHAPTER 7
DISCRIMINATION IN HOUSING
SECTION:
6-7-1: Adoption Of Federal Regulations; Enforcement
6-7-2: Regulations Posted
6-7-3: Booklets And Forms Available
6-7-1: ADOPTION OF FEDERAL REGULATIONS; ENFORCEMENT:
The Village hereby adopts by reference the rules and regulations regarding fair
housing issued by the Department of Housing and Urban Development and shall
enforce fair housing standards that comply with and/or are in accordance with
the Fair Housing Rules and Regulations of the U.S. Department of Housing and
Urban Development. (2018 Code)
6-7-2: REGULATIONS POSTED:
The Village will cause to be posted, in the offices of the Village and at other
places in the Village Hall, notices and fair housing posters advising the
public of the fair housing standards to be enforced in the Village. (2018 Code)
6-7-3: BOOKLETS AND FORMS AVAILABLE:
Complaint forms and booklets will be made available to the public and will
remain on file in the Village office for the benefit of the public, and the
Village shall provide any member of the public complaining of discrimination in
housing sufficient complaint forms to complete the process of such complaints.
(2018 Code)

CHAPTER 3
RECREATIONAL VEHICLES
SECTION:
7-3-1: Intent
7-3-2: Definition
7-3-3: Operation Restrictions
7-3-4: Penalty
7-3-1: INTENT:
It is the intent of the Board of Trustees to ensure the safety of residents and
their property. (Ord., 3-4-1995)
7-3-2: DEFINITION:
The following are considered recreational vehicles and shall apply to the
interpretation and enforcement of this chapter: all terrain vehicles (which
includes all wheels, 3 wheel, 4 wheel, and 6 wheel), motor scooters, minibikes,
go-carts, and snowmobiles. (Ord., 3-4-1995; amd. 2018 Code)
7-3-3: OPERATION RESTRICTIONS:
It shall be unlawful to operate a recreational vehicle within the Village
limits, except for the purpose of making their way out of the Village limits by
means of Willow Street or Maple Street. While in the Village limits, speed is
not to exceed fifteen (15) miles per hour. (Ord., 3-4-1995)
7-3-4: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be
fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., 3-4-1995; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 4
GOLF CARTS
SECTION:
7-4-1: Definitions
7-4-2: Registration And Permit Requirements
7-4-3: Insurance Required
7-4-4: Licensed Driver Required
7-4-5: Operation Regulations
7-4-6: Types Of Carts Allowed
7-4-7: State Regulations Adopted And Apply
7-4-8: Penalties
7-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
Any terms not otherwise defined in this chapter shall have the meanings as set
forth in the Illinois Vehicle Code 1 . (Ord. 10-1, 1-1-2010)
 
Notes
1 1. 625 ILCS 5/100 et seq.
7-4-2: REGISTRATION AND PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Registration And Permit Required: The Village shall require all golf
carts operated within the Village to be registered with the Village, display a
Village permit decal and a registration number on both sides of the golf cart
and one on the rear using three inch (3") reflective numbers.
   B.   Application For Permit; Fee: The application form will be maintained at
the Village Hall and a copy forwarded to the Village Police Committee
Chairperson. The yearly permit fee will be ten dollars ($10.00) per cart.
   C.   Affixing Decals And Numbers: Decals and numbers will be affixed by the
Village Police Committee Chairperson at the Village Hall or other predetermined
locations (i.e., residence, repair shop, etc.).
   D.   Suspension Or Revocation Of Permit: The Village shall maintain the
right to suspend or revoke the permit of any golf cart based on unsafe
operation or three (3) complaints during a six (6) month time period. All
complaints will be brought before the Village Board by the Police Committee
Chairperson. The Village Board, after reviewing the facts, may suspend or
revoke the permit. Suspensions will be in thirty (30) day increments. (Ord. 10-
1, 1-1-2010)
7-4-3: INSURANCE REQUIRED:
The Village shall require all registered golf carts to be insured and proof of
insurance to be carried at all times during operation (recreational vehicle
insurance). A copy of the insurance will be provided to the Village at the time
of registration. (Ord. 10-1, 1-1-2010)
7-4-4: LICENSED DRIVER REQUIRED:
Subject to the terms hereof, it shall be lawful for any person who is a
licensed driver to drive or operate a golf cart on all roadways within the
corporate limits of the Village, unless such roadway(s) is under the
jurisdiction of another unit of government which has not adopted legislation
allowing the operation of such golf carts. (Ord. 10-1, 1-1-2010; amd. 2018
Code)
7-4-5: OPERATION REGULATIONS:
   A.   Compliance With State Law; Headlights Required: The operation of a golf
cart on the roadways herein described, including operation of a golf cart after
sunset and before sunrise, shall be in compliance with the provisions of the
Illinois Rules of the Road and the Illinois Vehicle Code 1 . Headlights will be
required during all operation of the golf cart within the Village on any
roadway or alley. (Ord. 10-1, 1-1-2010)
   B.   Speed Limit: All golf carts registered within the Village will be
required to go no faster than fifteen (15) miles per hour. (Ord. 10-1, 1-1-
2010; amd. 2018 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. 625 ILCS 5/1-100 et seq.
7-4-6: TYPES OF CARTS ALLOWED:
All golf carts operated within the Village may be either/or electric or gas
operated. (Ord. 10-1, 1-1-2010)
7-4-7: STATE REGULATIONS ADOPTED AND APPLY:
   A.   All provisions set forth in the Illinois Vehicle Code 1  be and hereby
are adopted by reference and made a part of this chapter.
   B.   The provisions contained herein shall be in accordance with the terms
and provisions of the Illinois Rules of the Road and the Illinois Vehicle Code,
as may be amended from time to time. (Ord. 10-1, 1-1-2010)
 
Notes
1 2. 625 ILCS 5/1-100 et seq.
7-4-8: PENALTIES:
Any person operating a golf cart in the Village in violation of this chapter
shall be subject to fines and penalties prescribed under the Illinois Vehicle
Code or Village ordinance. Village ordinance fine shall be as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this Code, with review by Village Board for possible suspension of the
permit. (Ord. 10-1, 1-1-2010; amd. 2018 Code)
TITLE 8
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
8-1-1: Supervision And Enforcement
8-1-2: Construction Requirements
8-1-3: Maintenance Requirements
8-1-4: Use Of Public Ways
8-1-5: Excavations
8-1-6: Barricades
8-1-7: Deposits On Streets And Sidewalks
8-1-8: Utility Poles And Wires
8-1-9: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
8-1-10: Nuisances Declared
8-1-1: SUPERVISION AND ENFORCEMENT:
All public streets, alleys, sidewalks and other public ways in the Village
shall be under the supervision of the Committee on Streets and Alleys. It shall
have supervision over all work thereon, and shall have power to enforce all
ordinance provisions relating to such public places, and is hereby authorized
to enforce such ordinances. (1987 Code §
7-1-1)
8-1-2: CONSTRUCTION REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permit Requirements: It shall be unlawful to construct or lay any
pavement on any public street, sidewalk, alley or other public way, or to
repair the same, without first having secured a permit therefor. Applications
for such permits shall be made to the Clerk, and shall state the location of
the intended pavement or repair, the extent thereof, and the person who is to
do the actual construction work. No such permit shall be issued except on order
of the Committee on Streets and Alleys.
   B.   Bond Required: Each applicant shall file a bond in an amount to be
fixed by the Committee on Streets and Alleys, adequate to protect the Village,
with surety to be approved by said committee, conditioned to indemnify the
Village for any loss or damage resulting from the work undertaken or the manner
of doing the same.
   C.   Specifications: All street and sidewalk pavements shall be made in
conformity with the specifications laid down or approved from time to time by
the Board of Trustees. (1987 Code §
7-1-2)
8-1-3: MAINTENANCE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Repair Required: All public street, alley and sidewalk pavements shall
be kept in good repair. Such repair work, whether done by the Village or by the
abutting owner, shall be under the supervision of the Committee on Streets and
Alleys.
   B.   Duty Of Village Personnel: It shall be the duty of every Village
officer or employee, becoming cognizant of any defect in any street, alley or
sidewalk, or any obstruction thereof, to report the same to the Chair of the
Streets and Alleys Committee of the Village Board or the Board of Trustees as
soon as possible. (1987 Code § 7-1-3)
8-1-4: USE OF PUBLIC WAYS:
   A.   Sale Of Goods; Advertising: It shall be unlawful for any person to use
any street, sidewalk or other public place as space for the display or sale of
goods or merchandise; or to write or mark any signs or advertisements on any
such pavements.
   B.   Fences:
      1.   Encroaching Into Public Ways Prohibited: No person shall make, or
cause to be made, any enclosure, fence, bridge, arched way or building of any
kind extending upon, over or across any street, avenue, alley or sidewalk
within the Village.
      2.   Barbed Wire, Electric Fences: It shall be unlawful to construct or
renew any fence composed in whole or in part of barbed wire, or with any
similar material designed to cause injury to persons, or any wire charged with
electric current, anywhere within three feet (3') of any public street,
sidewalk, alley, park or other public way or place.
   C.   Gasoline Pumps: It shall be unlawful to erect any gasoline pump or tank
in any public street, alley or sidewalk.
   D.   Playing Games: It shall be unlawful to play any games upon any street,
alley or sidewalk, where such games cause unnecessary noise, or interfere with
traffic or pedestrians.
   E.   Coasting: It shall be unlawful for any person to indulge in the sport
commonly called coasting in or upon any of the public streets, avenues, alleys
or sidewalks of the Village. (1987 Code § 7-1-4)
8-1-5: EXCAVATIONS:
It shall be unlawful to make any excavation in or tunnel under any public
street, alley, sidewalk or other public place in the Village without having
first secured a permit therefor. Applications for such permits shall be made to
the Village Clerk, and shall specify the intended location and purpose of the
excavation. No permit shall be issued until the applicant has given the Village
a bond with adequate surety, indemnifying the Village for all liability arising
out of said excavation or tunneling. (1987 Code § 7-1-5)
8-1-6: BARRICADES:
   A.   Repairing Pavement: Any person laying or repairing any pavement on a
street, sidewalk or other public place, or making any excavation in any such
place, shall maintain suitable barricades to prevent injury to any person or
vehicle by reason of the work. Such barricades shall be protected by a light at
nighttime.
   B.   Defects In Pavement: Any defects in any pavement shall be barricaded to
prevent any injury, and any person properly maintaining any opening or
excavation in any such place shall guard such opening or excavation while the
same remains open by proper barricades and lights.
   C.   Disturbing Barricades: It shall be unlawful to disturb or interfere
with any barricade or light lawfully placed to protect or mark any new pavement
or opening in any public street, alley or sidewalk. (1987 Code § 7-1-6)
8-1-7: DEPOSITS ON STREETS AND SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Deposits On Streets:
      1.   Generally: No person shall place or throw any stone or sticks, logs,
stumps, manure or other articles, rubbish or materials in, over or upon any
street, avenue, alley or highway of the Village so as to obstruct the travel,
endanger life or limb or cause the destruction of property; or throw or deposit
manure, ashes, dirt or rubbish of any kind in the gutters of the Village. (1987
Code §
9-1-8)
      2.   Injurious Materials: It shall be unlawful to deposit on any street
any material which may be harmful to the pavement thereof, or any waste
material, or any glass, or other articles which may do injury to any person,
animal or property.
   B.   Deposits On Sidewalks: It shall be unlawful to deposit on any sidewalk
any material which may be harmful to the pavement thereof, or any waste
material, or any glass or other articles which might cause injury to persons,
animals or property. (1987 Code § 7-1-7; amd. 2018 Code)
8-1-8: UTILITY POLES AND WIRES:
   A.   Poles To Be Authorized: No person shall set or cause to be set any
telephone, electric light or other poles upon any street or alley, unless
authorized to do so by the Committee on Streets and Alleys.
   B.   Construction And Maintenance Requirements: In all new additions or
subdivisions, all telephone and electric light or power lines shall be
constructed and maintained in alleys or underground conduits. All guy wires
shall be equipped with guards from the ground level to a distance of eight feet
(8') above the ground level.
   C.   Location:
      1.   Poles: All electric light and telephone poles now in any street of
the Village, or which shall hereafter be placed on any alley or street, shall
be located and placed within the curb lines on the sidewalk side thereof, which
are now or may hereafter be established; and poles shall be placed as near as
may be in a line in such streets.
      2.   Wires: All wires suspended from utility poles shall be at least
thirty feet (30') high above the level of the street grade, and said poles
shall be neatly smoothed and in a fit condition to be painted. All high tension
wires shall, so far as practicable, be kept upon opposite sides of the streets
from telephone wires. (1987 Code § 7-1-8; amd. 2018 Code)
8-1-9: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Obstructions Generally: It shall be unlawful for any person to cause,
create or maintain any obstruction of any street, alley, sidewalk or other
public way, except as may be specifically authorized by ordinance or by the
Committee on Streets and Alleys.
   B.   Encroachments: It shall be unlawful to erect or maintain any building
or structure which encroaches upon any public street or property.
   C.   Injury To Pavements:
      1.   Generally: It shall be unlawful to injure any sidewalk, street or
alley pavements.
      2.   New Pavements: It shall be unlawful to walk upon or drive any
vehicle or animal upon, or injure any newly laid street or sidewalk pavement,
while the same is guarded by a warning sign or barricade, or to knowingly
injure any soft, newly laid pavement.
   D.   Removal Of Dirt And Gravel: It shall be unlawful for any private
purpose, for any person to dig, remove or carry away any earth, gravel or sod
from any street, avenue or alley, without first having secured the permission
of the Committee on Streets and Alleys.
   E.   Obstructing Drains: It shall be unlawful to obstruct any drains in any
public street or alley. (1987 Code § 7-1-9)
8-1-10: NUISANCES DECLARED:
All obstructions to streets, alleys, crossings and sidewalks of the Village and
all excavations in or under the same, which are by ordinance prohibited or
which may be made without lawful permission, are hereby declared to be
nuisances; and the persons erecting, keeping or maintaining any such
obstructions shall, in addition to any penalty specifically provided against
the same, be subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1987 Code § 7-1-10; amd. 2018 Code)
CHAPTER 2
VILLAGE PARKS
SECTION:
8-2-1: Park Hours
8-2-2: Penalty
8-2-1: PARK HOURS:
The following are the closing times of the parks:
Sunday through Thursday: Ten thirty o'clock (10:30) P.M.
Friday and Saturday: Eleven thirty o'clock (11:30) P.M. (Ord., 7-13-1996)
8-2-2: PENALTY:
Any person who violates the hours set out in section
8-2-1 of this chapter and is found guilty, upon conviction, shall be fined
according to the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., 7-13-1996)
CHAPTER 3
WATER USE AND SERVICE
SECTION:
8-3-1: Waterworks System
8-3-2: Application For Water And Connection To System
8-3-3: Supplying Water To Or Sales Of Water To Others Prohibited
8-3-4: Water Rates And Charges
8-3-5: Use Of Water And Payment Of Bills
8-3-6: General Rules And Regulations For Customers And Plumbers
8-3-7: Penalty
8-3-1: WATERWORKS SYSTEM:
In order to provide for the distribution of water by the Village, there shall
continue to be a waterworks system of the Village to be known as the
"Buckingham waterworks system", and the President is hereby authorized to
appoint, subject to the confirmation of the Board of Trustees, a water operator
of the Buckingham waterworks system, and all other necessary employees. The
water operator shall be under the general supervision of the Village Board of
Trustees. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012; amd. 2018 Code)
8-3-2: APPLICATION FOR WATER AND CONNECTION TO SYSTEM:
   A.   Application For Service; Deposit Required:
      1.   No water shall be turned on for use on or in any premises until an
application therefor in writing has been made for that purpose, and application
approved by the Village. As evidence of the applicant's intention to abide by
the provisions of the application and to purchase water at the established
rate, there shall be deposited with the application, in cash, or negotiable
check to the Village of Buckingham, the amount of sixty five dollars ($65.00),
which is nonrefundable and which shall be deposited by the Village and retained
as a guarantee of payment for water, as long as water usage by the customer
shall continue, or applied in payment of any delinquent account at any time, as
hereinafter provided.
      2.   Owners, tenants, or nonowners who are occupants of real estate to
which water is supplied will be required to deposit the sum of sixty five
dollars ($65.00) with the Village, which is nonrefundable. If the owner/
landlord keeps water in owner's/landlord's name, then there will be only one
(1) $65.00-turn on fee. If the name on the account changes, there will be a
sixty five dollar ($65.00) turn on fee whenever the name on the account
changes.
   B.   Unauthorized Turning On Of Water: No person, not duly authorized, shall
turn the water on at any fire hydrant or service cock, or use water therefrom,
when so turned on.
   C.   Plumbing To Comply With Village Regulations; Exception: No water shall
be turned on for service in premises to which plumbing does not comply with the
ordinances of the Village or the Illinois Plumbing Code, 77 Illinois
Administrative Code 890; provided, that water may be turned on for construction
work to unfinished buildings, subject to provisions of this chapter, by reason
of failure or breaking of any well main, branches, service pipe, apparatus or
appurtenances connected with said system or plant, or any part or portion of
said plant, or for any interruption of the supply by reason of the breakage of
machinery or by reason of stoppage, alteration, extension or renewals.
   D.   Responsibility Of Applicants And Owners:
      1.   All applicants for water service shall provide all service pipes and
appurtenances from the main to the premises to be served, at applicants' own
cost. Such installations shall be made under the direction of the Water
Department, and all service connections shall conform to the specifications of
the Board of Trustees and the Illinois Plumbing Code, 77 Illinois
Administrative Code 890, a copy of which shall be kept on file with the Village
Clerk and open to inspection for any interested person.
      2.   All repairs for service pipes and the plumbing system of buildings
to be served on the customer's premises shall be made by or at the expense of
the owner of the premises served. The Village may, in case of emergency, repair
any service pipe, and if this is done, the cost of such repair work shall be
repaid to the Village by the owner of the premises served. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-
2012)
   E.   Cross Connection Control: Any new water service connection or repair of
the water service connection will be in accordance with the Village cross
connection ordinance. An approved backflow, prevention device, in accordance
with the cross connection ordinance, will be installed at the water customer's
own expense, which customer will install such approved device at a location and
in a manner in accordance with the Illinois Plumbing Code, Illinois
Environmental Protection Agency and all applicable local regulations and shall
have inspections and tests made of such approved devices upon installation.
(Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012; amd. 2018 Code)
   F.   Nonmetered Service: A curb stop and access box for nonmetered service
shall be placed in every service pipe and shall be located between the curb
lines and the property line where practicable. Such boxes shall be located so
that they are easily accessible and shall be protected from frost.
   G.   Nonliability Of Village: All connections and water applied for
hereunder, and all the water used hereunder, shall be made upon the express
condition the Village shall not be liable, nor shall any claim be made against
it, for damages or injury caused. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012)
8-3-3: SUPPLYING WATER TO OR SALES OF WATER TO OTHERS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Supplying Water: No owner or occupant of any premises to which the
utility furnishes water will be allowed to supply water to any other persons or
families, or to haul water from the water system. Any owner or occupant
violating this subsection will be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code for each person or family so furnished with water, and if
not paid, the water supply shall be cut off from said premises. No consumer
shall be permitted to conduct water pipes or hoses across lots or buildings to
adjoining premises. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012; amd. 2018 Code)
   B.   Sales Of Water: No water shall be resold or distributed by the
recipient thereof from the Village supply to any premises or other person other
than that for which application has been made and facilities installed, except
in case of emergency. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012)
8-3-4: WATER RATES AND CHARGES:
   A.   Water Taps: The fee due the Village for new water connections shall be
four hundred dollars ($400.00).
   B.   User Rates:
      1.   Residential Water And Garbage Service:
 
a. Inside Village limits: Monthly rates per residential water services $42.00
   connection with garbage
  Water                                                               26.00
  Garbage                                                             16.00
b. Outside Village limits:                                             44.00
  Water                                                               28.00
  Garbage                                                             16.00
 
      2.   Commercial Or Business Or Industrial Water Service Connection;
Garbage Service:
 
Monthly rates per commercial or industrial water service connection $44.00
 Water                                                             28.00
 Garbage                                                           16.00
 
      3.   Business And Residence In Same Building: When a business and
residence installation is used in the same building, they shall be charged as
two (2) separate installations. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012)
8-3-5: USE OF WATER AND PAYMENT OF BILLS:
All water customers shall be supplied directly by the Village and shall pay for
the water at the current rates.
   A.   Monthly Payments; Liability: Rates or charges for water service shall
be payable monthly. The owner of the premises, occupant thereof and the user of
the service shall be jointly and severally liable to pay for the service to
such premises, and the service is furnished to the premises by the Village only
upon the condition that the owner of the premises, occupant and user of the
services are jointly and severally liable therefor to the Village.
   B.   Rendition Of Bills; Late Payment Fee: Bills for water service shall be
sent out by the Village Clerk each month and payable by the twentieth of the
month billed. A service charge of fifteen dollars ($15.00) per month shall be
added to all bills not paid by the due date.
   C.   Delinquent Payments; Lien Provisions: If the charges for such services
are not paid by the thirtieth day of the month succeeding the period for which
the service is billed, such charges shall be deemed delinquent. Delinquent
charges shall constitute liens upon the real estate to which the water services
were furnished. Whenever a bill for water service remains unpaid for sixty (60)
days after billing, the Village Clerk can file with the County Recorder of
Deeds a notice of such lien. This statement shall contain the legal description
of the premises served, the amount of the unpaid bill, and a notice that the
Village claims a lien for this amount as well as for all charges subsequent to
the period covered by the bill. If the user whose bill is unpaid is not the
owner of the premises and the Village Clerk has notice of this, notice shall be
mailed to the owner of the premises if his address is known to the Clerk,
whenever such bill remains unpaid for the period of sixty (60) days after
billing. The failure of the Village Clerk to record such lien or to mail such
notice or the failure of the owner to receive such notice shall not affect the
right to foreclose the lien for unpaid bills.
   D.   Discontinuance Of Service: In addition to the remedies set forth in
subsection C of this section, the Village, after giving notice to the owner,
occupant or user by certified mail or personal service or posting notice on the
premises and providing other procedural protections consistent with the
requirements of due process, may discontinue water service to any premises for
which the owner, occupant or user is delinquent in the payment of water service
charges. An administrative charge of ten percent (10%) of the past due
delinquent bill will be assessed for delinquent notice served by certified mail
or personal service or posting notice on the premises. Water service shall be
resumed upon payment of the delinquent charges in full, administrative charges,
plus payment of sixty five dollars ($65.00) to defray the expense of
reinstating water service if necessary and the actual cost to the Village to
disconnect and to reinstate water service if necessary.
   E.   Termination Of Service By User: Any user requesting a termination of
service shall give written notice to the Village ten (10) days prior to the
time such termination of service is desired. Responsibility for payment for
water service prior to the date of termination shall be jointly with the
property owners as well as the user.
   F.   Entry Powers For Examining And Testing System: The Village and its
employees shall have ready access to the premises, places or buildings where
water is supplied, for the purpose of examining and testing consumption, use
and flow of water, and it shall be unlawful for any person or corporation to
interfere with, prevent, or obstruct the Village or its employees in its or
their duties hereunder.
   G.   Metered Service May Be Required: The Village reserves the right to
meter any customer at any time it deems it necessary for the proper operation
of the system. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012)
8-3-6: GENERAL RULES AND REGULATIONS FOR CUSTOMERS AND PLUMBERS:
   A.   Obstructing System Prohibited:
      1.   No person shall in any manner obstruct the access to any stopcock,
hydrant or valve, or any public faucet or opening for taking water in any
street, alley, public ground or place connected with, or part of said water
system, nor pile or place lumber, brick, building materials, trash or other
articles or things whatsoever within twelve feet (12') of the same, as to in
any way or manner hinder, delay or obstruct the members of the Water Department
or Fire Department in reaching the same.
      2.   It shall be unlawful for any person in any manner to interfere with
or obstruct the flow, retention, storage or authorized use of water, or
contaminate the water, in said water system, reservoir or plant, or any part
thereof, or to injure, deface, or displace any water main, hydrant, service
pipe, water system or plant, or to cause, suffer or permit any of said things
to be done.
   B.   Damage To, Tampering With System: It shall be unlawful for any person
not authorized by the Village to tamper with, alter, or injure any part of the
Village waterworks or supply system.
   C.   Authority Of Village To Shut Off Service: The Village reserves the
right to shut off water at any time in the mains for the purpose of repairing,
cleaning, making connections with or extensions to same, or for concentrating
water in any part of the Village in case of fire, and for restricting the use
of water in case of deficiency in supply. No claim shall be made against the
Village by reason of the breaking of any service pipe or any service pipecock,
or damage arising from shutting off the water for repairing, laying or relaying
mains, hydrants or other connections or repairing any part of the water system,
or from the failure of the water supply, or by increasing the water pressure at
any time, or from concentration or restricted use of water as above.
   D.   Emergency Conservation Measures: The right is reserved to suspend the
use of lawn fountains and hoses for sprinkling lawns and gardens, whenever, in
the opinion of the Board of Trustees, public emergencies require it.
   E.   Violation Of Rules; Nonpayment Of Bills: For the violation of any of
the foregoing rules or for the nonpayment of water bills, the Village reserves
the right to turn off the water without notice and to forfeit any payments
made, and after an account of nonpayment of water bills or violation of the
rules, the same will not be turned on again until all delinquent bills and
penalties are paid, together with the expense of turning off and on such water,
and no water will be furnished to any person who is indebted to the Village on
account of water consumed, material or repairs. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012)
8-3-7: PENALTY:
Any person or corporation who shall violate any of the rules and regulations
provided in this chapter shall, upon conviction, in addition to the enforcement
of the forfeitures and liabilities and attorney fees and liens therein
contained, pay a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code, and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on each
day during, or on which, a violation occurs or continues. (Ord. 12-8, 3-5-2012;
amd. 2018 Code)
ARTICLE A. CROSS-CONNECTION CONTROL
SECTION:
8-3A-1: Cross-Connections Prohibited
8-3A-2: Surveys And Investigations
8-3A-3: Backflow Prevention Devices
8-3A-4: Entry Powers For Inspections
8-3A-5: Violation Procedures
8-3A-6: Responsibility For Cleanup Costs
8-3A-7: Additional Regulations Adopted
8-3A-1: CROSS-CONNECTIONS PROHIBITED:
No person, firm or corporation shall establish or permit to be established or
maintain or permit to be maintained any connection whereby a private, auxiliary
or emergency water supply other than the regular public water supply of the
Village enters the supply or distribution system of the Village, unless such
private, auxiliary or emergency water supply and the method of connection and
use of such supply shall have been approved by the Superintendent of Water and
the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency. (Ord. 02-12, 12-23-2002, eff. 12-
23-2002)
8-3A-2: SURVEYS AND INVESTIGATIONS:
It shall be the duty of the Superintendent of Water to cause surveys and
investigations to be made of industrial and other properties served by the
public water supply to determine whether actual or potential hazards to the
public water supply may exist. Such surveys and investigations shall be made a
matter of public record and shall be repeated at least every two (2) years, or
as often as the Superintendent of Water shall deem necessary. Records of such
surveys shall be maintained and available for review for a period of at least
five (5) years. (Ord. 02-12, 12-23-2002, eff. 12-23-2002)
8-3A-3: BACKFLOW PREVENTION DEVICES:
All plumbing installed within the Village shall be installed in accordance with
the Illinois Plumbing Code, 77 Illinois Administrative Code 890. If, in
accordance with the Illinois Plumbing Code or in the judgment of the
Superintendent of Water, an approved backflow prevention device is necessary
for the safety of the public water supply system, the Superintendent of Water
will give notice to the water customer to install such an approved device
immediately. The water customer shall, at his own expense, install such an
approved device at a location and in a manner in accordance with the Illinois
Plumbing Code and all applicable local regulations, and shall have inspections
and tests made of such approved devices upon installation and as required by
the Illinois Plumbing Code and local regulations. (Ord. 02-12, 12-23-2002, eff.
12-23-2002)
8-3A-4: ENTRY POWERS FOR INSPECTIONS:
The approved cross-connection control device inspector shall have the right to
enter at any reasonable time any property served by a connection to the public
water supply or distribution system of the Village for the purpose of verifying
the presence or absence of cross-connections, and the Water Superintendent or
his authorized agent shall have the right to enter at any reasonable time any
property served by a connection to the public water supply or distribution
system of the Village for the purpose of verifying information submitted by the
customer regarding the required cross-connection control inspection. On demand,
the owner, lessees or occupants of any property so served shall furnish to the
Superintendent of Water any information which he may request regarding the
piping system or systems or water use on such property. The refusal of such
information, when demanded, shall, with the discretion of the Superintendent of
Water, be deemed evidence of the presence of improper connections as provided
in this article. (Ord. 02-12, 12-23-2002, eff. 12-23-2002)
8-3A-5: VIOLATION PROCEDURES:
The Village Superintendent of Water is hereby advised and directed to
discontinue, after reasonable notice to the occupant thereof, the water service
to any user wherein any connection in violation of the provisions of this
article is known to exist, and to take such precautionary measures as he may
deem necessary to eliminate any danger of contamination of the public water
supply distribution mains. Water service to such property shall not be restored
until such conditions have been eliminated or corrected in compliance with the
provisions of this article, and until a reconnection fee of sixty five dollars
($65.00) is paid to the Village. Immediate disconnection with verbal notice can
be effected when the Superintendent of Water is assured that imminent danger of
harmful contamination of the public water supply system exists. Such action
shall be followed by written notification of the cause of disconnection.
Immediate disconnection without notice to any party can be effected to prevent
actual or anticipated contamination or pollution of the public water supply;
provided, that in the reasonable opinion of the Superintendent of Water or the
Illinois Environmental Protection Agency, such action is required to prevent
actual or potential contamination or pollution of the public water supply.
Neither the public water supply, the Superintendent of Water, or his agents or
assigns shall be liable to any customer for any injury, damages or lost
revenues which may result from termination of said customer's water supply in
accordance with the terms of this article, whether or not said termination was
with or without notice. (Ord. 02-12, 12-23-2002, eff. 12-23-2002)
8-3A-6: RESPONSIBILITY FOR CLEANUP COSTS:
The consumer responsible for backsiphoned material or contamination through
backflow if contamination of the potable water supply system occurs through an
illegal cross-connection or an improperly installed, maintained or repaired
device, or a device which has been bypassed, must bear the cost of cleanup of
the potable water supply system. (Ord. 02-12, 12-23-2002, eff. 12-23-2002)
8-3A-7: ADDITIONAL REGULATIONS ADOPTED:
There are hereby adopted by reference those regulations entitled "Suggested
Municipal/Private Water Company Regulations on Cross- Connection Control"
attached to ordinance 02-12. Copies of said regulations are on file in the
Office of the Village Clerk for public use and inspection. (2018 Code)
TITLE 9
BUILDING AND DEVELOPMENT
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL BUILDING REGULATIONS; ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
9-1-1: Code Enforcement Officer
9-1-2: Permit Requirements
9-1-3: Demolition Of Buildings
9-1-4: Fees
9-1-5: Variations
9-1-6: Stop Work Orders
9-1-7: Notice Of Violation; Failure To Comply
9-1-8: Penalties
9-1-1: CODE ENFORCEMENT OFFICER:
   A.   Office Created; Residency; Appointment: The office of code enforcement
officer is hereby created, who shall be a qualified individual or consulting
agency or firm and appointed by the Village President, with the consent of the
Board of Trustees. (1987 Code § 1-7D-1)
   B.   Duties:
      1.   It shall be the duty of the code enforcement officer to enforce all
ordinances and laws related to the construction, alteration, removal and
demolition of buildings and structures, together with electrical and plumbing
installations therein.
      2.   The code enforcement officer shall keep careful, systematic records
of the business and work of the office, including permit applications, survey
plats and building plot plans, all construction plans and specifications,
copies of permits and certificates issued, affidavits and certificates
received, a record of inspections, copies of notices and orders issued and
reports of tests made.
      3.   The code enforcement officer is hereby authorized to make
inspections to enforce the provisions of the Village building regulations and
for such purposes is hereby authorized to enter any building, structure or
premises.
      4.   The code enforcement officer shall retain plans and specifications
of houses and accessories, except survey plats and building plot plans for a
period of two (2) years. Parts of plans for other buildings which may be useful
for future periodic inspections shall also be retained.
   C.   Vacancy In Office: The Chair of the Planning and Zoning Committee of
the Board of Trustees will act as code enforcement officer during periods in
which the appointed building inspector is absent from the Village or during
periods when a vacancy in the office of building inspector exists.
   D.   Compensation: The compensation for the code enforcement officer shall
be as determined by the Village Board of Trustees. (1987 Code §§ 1-7D-2 - 1-7D-
4; amd. 2018 Code; Ord., 9-5-2023)
9-1-2: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permit Required: No new construction or building shall be permitted
within the Village limits, and no new additions to, improvements on or
replacements of existing buildings or structures shall be permitted within the
Village limits unless the person responsible for said construction or building,
or the owner of the property upon which the construction or building is to be
erected, added or replaced, or both, shall first obtain from the code
enforcement officer as appointed by the Village Board of Trustees a permit
authorizing the contemplated construction, addition or replacement.
   B.   Application For Permit: Any person desiring to so construct or build a
new building or structure or to add to, alter, improve or replace an existing
building within the Village limits shall first file with the code enforcement
officer or, in the event the position of code enforcement officer is vacant,
Chair of the Planning and Zoning Committee an application for permit, together
with such fees as are hereinafter prescribed, which application shall contain:
      1.   Detailed plans and specifications of the proposed construction,
addition, improvement, or replacement.
      2.   A sketch showing the location of the proposed construction,
addition, improvement or replacement upon the lot or lots on which the same is
to be made and, in particular, showing the distance of the proposed
construction from the lot lines involved.
      3.   The use or purposes for which the proposed construction is intended;
whether a residence, garage or business property; and if a residence,
specifying the number of families to be housed therein, or if a business
building, the type of business to be conducted therein.
      4.   The name and address of the owner of record of the lot or lots upon
which the proposed construction is to be placed and the consent of such owner
to such proposed construction, provided the application is submitted by any
person other than said owner.
      5.   The name and address of the person who is to perform the proposed
construction, together with an estimate of the reasonable costs of such
proposed construction.
   C.   Construction Requirements: Upon submission of any application for
permit to the code enforcement officer as hereinbefore provided, such permit
shall be granted in accordance with the terms of the application, provided the
application shows that the proposed construction will comply with the
following:
      1.   Floor Area: All new construction, including replacements of existing
structures for residential purposes, shall contain a minimum of seven hundred
fifty (750) square feet of floor space for a single-family dwelling and one
thousand five hundred (1,500) square feet for a multi-family dwelling,
breezeways, porches, garages and basements excluded.
      2.   Location:
         a.   Except as herein provided, no construction, addition, improvement
or replacement shall be located nearer than five feet (5') to the side lot
lines nor ten feet (10') to the front and back lot lines, provided construction
is contemplated on one lot, and further provided, that where the proposed
construction is to be located on more than one lot, the above setbacks shall
apply to the outer lot lines of the lots involved.
         b.   In the event the proposed construction is to be used as a garage,
said construction shall be not nearer than five feet (5') to the side lot lines
and ten feet (10') to the front lot line.
         c.   In the event the proposed construction is to be used for business
purposes and in the event the application shall contain a request for variation
in the above restrictions, the Board of Trustees may, in its discretion, allow
such variation, which shall be in compliance with subsection
10-3A-5 C of this Code.
      3.   Number Of Buildings Per Lot: No new building intended for
residential living shall be constructed on any lot upon which a building
intended for residential living is already located.
      4.   Animal Shelter: No construction intended for or used solely for the
maintenance, housing or care of animals and livestock, ordinary house pets
excepted, shall be permitted.
   D.   Each application for permit shall be approved or denied by the code
enforcement officer based on its satisfactory compliance with all adopted
building codes, Village ordinances, and State statutes. Appeals for denials
shall be heard by the Village Board of Trustees at their regularly scheduled
meeting and a final determination shall be made by the Village Board of
Trustees. (1987 Code §§ 4-1-1, 4-1-3, 4-1-5; amd. Ord., 6-1-1996; Ord. 17-7,
10-3-2017; 2018 Code; Ord., 9-5-2023)
9-1-3: DEMOLITION OF BUILDINGS:
   A.   Permit Required; Application: Any person desiring to demolish a
building or structure shall file first with the code enforcement officer or, in
the event the position of code enforcement officer is vacant, Chair of Planning
and Zoning Committee an application for permit which shall contain the
following:
      1.   A sketch showing the location of the proposed demolition. The sketch
will include locations of septic systems, cisterns, or buried fuel tanks.
      2.   The name and address of the owner of record of the lot or lots upon
which demolition is to take place and the consent of such owner to such
proposed demolition, provided the application is submitted by any person other
than the said owner.
      3.   The name and address of the person who is to perform the proposed
demolition.
   B.   Permit Fee And Bond And Insurance: A permit fee for demolition will be
fifty dollars ($50.00), plus a five thousand dollar ($5,000.00) surety bond and
evidence of liability insurance wherein the Village is a named insured in an
amount not less than five hundred thousand dollars ($500,000.00) for personal
injury or property damage.
   C.   Term Of Permit; Extensions: The approved permit is good for sixty (60)
days from date of issue. A request for a second time limit of sixty (60) days
will cost two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) and for any additional request
for the same property will be the same. Said permits shall expire sixty (60)
days from date of issuance unless otherwise provided in this Code. (Ord. 12-10,
3-5-2012; amd. 2018 Code; Ord., 9-5-2023)
9-1-4: FEES:
For the issuance of each building permit and for other miscellaneous subjects,
all fees shall be paid by the applicant to the Kankakee County Planning
Department. Unless specified elsewhere in the Village Code, all fees will be in
accordance with the fee schedule established by Kankakee County as amended
which is hereby incorporated into this chapter by reference.
   A.   Inspections:
      1.   All reinspection fees will be paid for by the property owner.
      2.   All open trenches for water and sewer must be inspected by the code
enforcement officer or designated plumbing inspector.
      3.   In new construction a backflow preventer device must be installed
and inspected according to the Illinois Plumbing Code.
      4.   Repaired water lines must be inspected by the code enforcement
officer or designated plumbing inspector.
   B.   Where work for which a permit is required under this chapter is started
or proceeded with prior to obtaining a permit, the fees herein set forth shall
be increased one hundred percent (100%). (Ord. 12-9, 3-5-2012; amd. 2018 Code;
Ord., 9-5-2023)
9-1-5: VARIATIONS:
It shall be unlawful to vary from the approved plans and specifications
deposited with and approved by the code enforcement officer unless amended
plans and specifications showing such proposed alteration and variation are
first filed with and approved by the code enforcement officer. If such
variation involves an increase in the total cost of the work, a statement to
that effect shall be made and the necessary additional fees shall be paid. The
variation procedure shall be in compliance with subsection
10-3A-5 C of this Code. (1987 Code § 4-1-8; amd. 2018 Code; Ord., 9-5-2023)
9-1-6: STOP WORK ORDERS:
The code enforcement officer may order work stopped whenever any construction,
alteration or repair work is being done in violation of this chapter. Such stop
order, when oral, shall be followed by a written stop order within twenty four
(24) hours. It shall be unlawful to continue with any work in violation of a
stop order until such order has been revoked by the person issuing it or by the
Village President or Board of Trustees. (1987 Code § 4-1-9; amd. Ord., 9-5-
2023)
9-1-7: NOTICE OF VIOLATION; FAILURE TO COMPLY:
If at any time after the effective date hereof, the Village Clerk shall find
that any person is engaged in construction without having first obtained a
permit, or any person who, holding a permit, is in violation of said permit in
any particular, it shall be the duty of the code enforcement officer to notify
such violator by posting a notice of violation on the property in a conspicuous
and accessible location. Said notice shall state the nature of the violation
and shall further state that unless there is compliance with the terms of this
chapter within thirty (30) days from the receipt of such notice, the violator
shall be subject to the fines and penalties hereinafter prescribed. If, upon
the expiration of such thirty (30) days, the code enforcement officer shall
find continued failure to comply, he shall revoke the permit in the case of
violation thereof and assess the fines and penalties hereinafter prescribed.
(1987 Code § 4-1-10; amd. Ord., 9-5-2023)
9-1-8: PENALTIES:
Any person who shall engage in construction of any type in violation of this
chapter shall be subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code, and in addition, each day or part thereof that the
violation shall continue after proper notice of such violation shall be
considered a separate and distinct violation hereof. However, nothing herein
contained shall be deemed to restrict any right of the Board of Trustees to
take whatever other action shall be considered necessary to secure compliance
with the terms of this chapter. (1987 Code § 4-1-11; amd. 2018 Code)

BUILDING CODES AND REGULATIONS

9-2-1: CODES AND REGULATIONS ADOPTED:

shall govern all matters covered therein to the extent that the same are not in
conflict with nor amended by any provision of this Code or other ordinances of
the Village. (Ord. 17-1, 1-3-2017)

ARTICLE A. PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE
SECTION:
9-2A-1: Code Adopted
9-2A-2: Amendments To Code
9-2A-1: CODE ADOPTED:
A certain document, three (3) copies of which are on file in the Office of the
Village Clerk, being marked and designated as the International Property
Maintenance Code, 2015 edition, as published by the International Code Council,
be and is hereby adopted as the Property Maintenance Code of the Village, for
regulating and governing the conditions and maintenance of all property,
buildings, and structures; by providing the standards for supplied utilities
and facilities and other physical things and conditions essential to ensure
that structures are safe, sanitary, and fit for occupation and use; and the
condemnation of buildings and structures unfit for human occupancy and use, and
the demolition of such existing structures as herein provided; providing for
the issuance of permits and collection of fees therefor; and each and all of
the regulations, provisions, penalties, conditions, and terms of said Property
Maintenance Code on file in the office of the Village are hereby referred to,
adopted, and made a part hereof, as if fully set out in this chapter, with the
additions, insertions, deletions, and changes, if any, prescribed in section
9-2A-2 of this article. (Ord. 17-2, 1-3-2017)
9-2A-2: AMENDMENTS TO CODE:
The following sections of the Code adopted in section
9-2A-1 of this article are hereby revised:
Section 101.1. Insert: Village of Buckingham.
Section 102.3. Application of other codes. Delete: "International Existing
Building Code" and replace with "International Building Code, International
Fuel Gas Code, International Mechanical Code, Illinois State Plumbing Code and
the National Electrical Code". Delete: "International Zoning Code" and replace
with "Buckingham Village Code".
Section 103.5. Fees. Insert: The fees for activities and services performed by
the Village of Buckingham and its departments in carrying out its
responsibilities under this code shall be as established by the governing body,
or as otherwise provided herein.
Section 201.3. Terms defined in other code. Delete: International Zoning Code,
International Plumbing Code, International Existing Building Code and ICC
Electrical Code, and Insert: Buckingham Village Code, Illinois State Plumbing
Code and National Electrical Code.
Section 302.4. Weeds. Insert: eight inches (8").
Section 304.14. Insect screens. Insert: April 1st to December 1st.
Chapter 5 Plumbing Facilities and Fixture Requirements. Delete: All references
to the International Plumbing Code and Insert: Illinois State Plumbing Code.
Chapter 6 Mechanical and Electrical Requirements. Delete: All reference to the
International Plumbing Code and ICC Electrical Code, and Insert: Illinois State
Plumbing Code and National Electrical Code.
Section 602.3. Heat supply. Insert: October 1st to May 15th.
Section 602.4. Heat supply. Insert: October 1st to May 15th.
(Ord. 17-2, 1-3-2017)
CHAPTER 3
DWELLING LICENSING PROVISIONS
SECTION:
9-3-1: Licensing Requirements
9-3-2: Inspections
9-3-3: Fire, Life, Health, And Safety Code Violations
9-3-4: Limit On Occupancy
9-3-5: Designation Of Manager/Agent
9-3-6: Tenant's Responsibilities
9-3-7: Minor Violations
9-3-8: Appeals
9-3-9: Penalty
9-3-1: LICENSING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required: No person, corporation or other entity shall rent,
lease or allow a person other than the legal owner to occupy any dwelling unit
within the Village, unless the Village has issued a current unrevoked operating
license in the name of the legal owner of record for that premises. (Ord. 12-
12, 3-12-2012)
   B.   Initial License: An initial operating license shall be issued upon the
inspection of the premises and the determination by the Village that the
premises is in compliance with the applicable Property Maintenance, Fire and
Life Safety Codes, as amended. Upon the issuance of an initial license, every
licensed premises shall require an annual inspection, unless revoked sooner or
as provided pursuant to the applicable sections of this chapter. (Ord. 12-12,
3-12-2012; amd. 2018 Code)
   C.   Application For License:
      1.   All applications for operating licenses shall be submitted on forms
provided by the Village along with a fee as hereinafter provided. In the event
that the legal owner of the premises designates a manager or agent other than
the legal owner to be responsible for the maintenance or leasing of said
premises, the name, address and phone number of the designated manager and/or
agent shall also be included upon the application and the application shall
also be verified by the manager/agent. The owner shall remain legally
responsible for the premises.
      2.   All applications for operating license shall include the name and
address of the tenants who are or will be residing in said dwelling unit and
the total number of persons residing in said unit. If the property has not been
leased at the time of the inspection, the license holder shall supply the names
of the tenants within thirty (30) days of the commencement date of the lease.
It is the duty of the license holder to supply the identity of the tenant
within thirty (30) days after a change of occupancy. A change of occupancy is
defined as the elimination of occupancy by one tenant and the initiation of
occupancy of the dwelling unit by a different tenant.
   D.   Lease Provisions: All applicants for operating licenses under this
chapter shall include in all written leases a provision which requires the
tenants to permit the inspection of the premises which is the subject matter of
the lease, said inspection to be conducted by a representative of the Village.
Said provision shall refer to section 104.4 IPMC. (Ord. 12-12, 3-12-2012)
   E.   Issuance Of License: If, upon reinspection, the Village determines that
the dwelling unit in connection with which the notice was issued for suspension
or revocation has come into compliance with all applicable codes, statutes,
rules and regulations, the Village shall issue an annual license. (Ord. 12-12,
3-12-2012; amd. 2018 Code)
   F.   Renewal Of License: No operating license may be renewed unless an
application therefor has been made prior to the expiration of the existing
operating license. In the event that a license is sought after the expiration
date of a current license, the applicant for the license shall pay an
additional fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for said license. Upon payment
of the fee and the property being determined to be in compliance with all
applicable rules, regulations and ordinances of the Village and the Statutes of
the State of Illinois, a license will thereupon be issued.
   G.   Nonassignability, Nontransferability Of License:
      1.   Any license issued pursuant to this chapter is nonassignable by the
holder thereof. Upon transfer of ownership of any premises subject to this
chapter, the new owner shall make application for a new rental license and be
subject to the terms of this chapter. A sale on contract is a "transfer" with
the meaning of this subsection.
      2.   No operating license shall be transferable to another person or
entity or another dwelling unit. Each person holding an unrevoked operating
license shall give notice, in writing, to the Village within ten (10) working
days after having transferred or otherwise disposing of the legal control of
any licensed dwelling unit. Such notice shall include the name and address or
persons succeeding to the ownership or control of such dwelling unit.
   H.   Revocation Of License; Effect:
      1.   An operating license which has been previously issued shall be
revoked if, following an inspection pursuant to this chapter, any dwelling unit
within a rental building fails to meet all applicable requirements of all codes
of the Village and Statutes of the State of Illinois. Upon the inspection
determining that said property fails to meet said codes, a "notice of
revocation" shall be issued. A copy of the notice of revocation shall be issued
to all tenants living within the property which is the subject matter of the
revocation. Upon notice of revocation, all tenants may be required to vacate
the premises which is the subject of the revoked license. A legal owner of
record may appeal the notice of revocation in accordance to the provisions set
forth in section
9-3-8 of this chapter.
      2.   If a license is revoked, the property or any individual dwelling
